Important News

Struggle of the Liaonan National Salvation Army 58

"Old North Wind" Shakes Haicheng

Japanese Residents Live in Unease

A correspondent from Beiping reports that people from Haicheng say that the Second Military Region's Liaonan National Salvation Army, since its launch in early August, rested briefly. Afterward, they received orders for a second general offensive, and began their second campaign in mid-August. For a month, they have not rested. The South Manchuria Railway stations in Liaoyang, Haicheng, Yingkou, Dashiqiao, and other places are their targets of attack, and they have repeatedly performed meritorious deeds. Recent combat situations are detailed below.

Four Attacks on Haicheng: Zhang Haitian (i.e., "Old North Wind") is a famous hero in western Liaoning. His troops attacked Haicheng three times: once during the general offensive on August 1, twice on the 3rd, and a third time on a certain day in mid-August. Each attack resulted in a safe retreat, but when the Japanese army attacked, they suffered harm instead, sometimes being surrounded. As a result, the Japanese military police, women, and children in Haicheng fear him like a tiger, constantly praying that Old North Wind will not come again. On the night of the 23rd, in a small village near Haicheng, a sick person sent to Chong set off firecrackers. The Japanese army suspected that Old North Wind had arrived again, and fled in panic. When dawn broke, they sent scouts to inquire and learned the truth, so they transferred their anger to the villagers and immediately used artillery fire to wash the village away. When Li Chunhua, acting commander-in-chief of the Second Military Region, learned of this, he truly sent Old North Wind to attack. On the 26th, they made contact with the Japanese army. At night, they attacked the South Manchuria Railway station. At this time, the Japanese army had moved its residents within the Japanese boundary into the garrison barracks, doing its best to protect them. Our army launched several fierce attacks, but due to the excessive Japanese artillery fire, they could not break in. They only destroyed and burned the buildings within the Japanese station boundary. The night sky was filled with firelight. By dawn, the Japanese essence of Haicheng had been largely destroyed by Zhang Haitian's four attacks.

Destroying the South Manchuria Railway: Dashiqiao manages transport to places like Yingkou, Lushun, and Shenyang and is of critical importance. As a result, the Japanese army recently transferred a regiment (regiment number unknown) from Lushun to be stationed there and strengthen defenses. Around 8:00 PM on the 25th, the insurgent army led by Yin Yuanmin emerged from Yuezhou Temple and, together with the independent contingent led by Kuang, advancing north from Tangchi, coordinated their attack. The Japanese army, because the momentum of the attack was fierce, had no strength to resist, and retreated into the trenches, crawling deep inside, daring not come out. However, using defensive works, they fired at the insurgent army with dense machine guns and small cannons. The insurgent army mostly rushed to the electric fence, cutting it open and breaking in. One part of the insurgent army controlled the Japanese army's advance, while the majority scattered around the east station of Dashiqiao, calmly dismantling the main railway lines to Yingkou, Lushun, and Shenyang, and firing dozens of cannons before leaving. Afterward, the Japanese army continued firing non-stop until dawn. After going out to inspect, they had wasted two hours' worth of bullets.

Stealthily Crossing the Liao River: As for the insurgent army in Yingkou, since receiving the order for the second general offensive, there has been contact every day from the 15th until now, with no day without fighting. To cut off the insurgent army's attacks, the Japanese army confiscated all ships within fifteen miles upstream and downstream of the Liao River, keeping them on the south bank to prevent the insurgent army from crossing. However, the insurgent army bypassed the Japanese forces near the reed marshes and stealthily crossed to the south bank, destroying the section of the South Manchuria Railway from Dashiqiao to Yingkou. As a result, the Yingkou branch line is sometimes impassable. In Liaoyang, battles have also occurred every day for the past half month. The two units of Wu Baofeng and Wang Quan have surrounded the western South Manchuria Railway station in Liaoyang, using a "wheel battle" tactic, taking turns attacking from the north and south every day. Gunfire is constant every night. Japanese military police sometimes go missing, much to the suffering of the Japanese. The insurgent army's activities in Yingkou and Liaoyang, with stealth crossings and rotating attacks, resemble tactics from the Middle Ages, making it an interesting story.

Japanese Panic: Secondly, in Liaoyang city, after Shang Jiyuan launched the burning of the Manchuria Spinning Factory warehouse, all Japanese employers of Chinese are in a precarious situation, fearing being harmed. As a result, Chinese workers in Japanese factories, shops, and homes are being dismissed. The Japanese army is also strictly inspecting the streets to prevent Chinese riots. At the same time, they suspect that the police are in contact with the volunteer army, so they have transferred all of them outside the city to attack the volunteer army. In the city, they have drawn strong men from various shops to form merchant corps, with Japanese serving as captains and squad leaders. However, the Japanese are overly suspicious and recently suspect that the merchant corps are also colluding with the enemy, and they are making arrests from time to time. Therefore, each merchant corps member is anxious, and thinks of defecting, with a situation that is about to explode.

Japanese Army Threatened: As for the small stations along the South Manchuria Railway, such as Tashan, Fenshui, Lishan, Tanggangzi, Yantai, and Hunhe, because of the activities of the insurgent army, South Manchuria Railway trains mostly pass with lights off. The insurgent army appears and disappears unpredictably. As for Xiang Zhongyi and Pei Jingkui in western Liaoning, they are preparing to attack Panshan, Dahushan, and Goubangzi. Deng Tiemei's unit in eastern Liaoning is approaching Benxi. The Japanese army is threatened on both sides (September 2nd).

General Headquarters Orders Hubei Provincial Government to Implement Austerity Policy 59

Monthly Government Expenses Not to Exceed 700,000

Six Measures Prescribed for Raising Bandit Suppression Funds

A correspondent from Hankou reports that regarding the problem of reorganizing Hubei Province's finances, the Three Provinces Bandit Suppression General Headquarters has sent personnel to investigate and formulate a plan. Yesterday, the Hubei Provincial Government received instructions from the General Headquarters to implement austerity policies, effective October 1st, and to implement a new budget. Six measures have also been drafted for raising bandit suppression funds, to achieve temporary reconciliation of income and expenditure. The original text of the instructions is as follows: "After investigating Hubei Province's local finances, the deficit has grown significantly. The Headquarters has sent personnel to investigate and hold meetings to discuss the current situation of income and expenditure, and determined a direction for reorganization: (A) Implement an austerity policy to seek a balance of regular income and expenditure. According to the Finance Department's report, monthly income is 1,194,500 yuan, and monthly expenditure is 1,893,964 yuan, with a monthly deficit of 700,000 yuan. If this continues, the annual deficit will be 8 million yuan, and the accumulated debt will be higher, making it more difficult to remedy. Fifteen years ago, Hubei Province's monthly government expenses were only 300,000 yuan. Even when Director Zhang took office, it was only 500,000 yuan, which was enough to maintain the current situation. It is up to the heads of the province to recognize that this kind of procrastinating is dangerous and ill-advised. Endure the pain for a while, implement an austerity policy, and adopt the principle of living within your means. Revise the new budget for the 21st year, and redistribute the monthly income of 1,194,500 yuan: (1) The total amount of monthly government expenses is limited to 700,000 yuan, which should be discussed by the provincial government and distributed separately among the various agencies and items. Matters related to education and security are important government affairs and should still have maintenance considered amidst the frugality; (2) According to the original Finance Department, another 300,000 yuan per month is used as a public debt fund and to repay loan principal and interest to protect credit. After the principal and interest are paid off, this amount will be used for provincial construction; (3) The remaining 194,500 yuan is the expense of the Security Office and the Administrative Inspector, and for temporary aftercare, rural restoration, and reform of public administration. To strictly implement the method of limiting monthly expenditure to 700,000 yuan, it is even more necessary to endure the pain and strictly implement the following three things: First, cut. Any redundant agencies or non-urgent matters that can be cut should be cut directly. Second, reduce. The expenses of all agencies or matters should be reduced at the same time, taking into account the actual situation. Third, merge. Any agencies or matters that can be merged should be merged and handled. The annual expenditure should be reduced to the predetermined standard based on this principle, and the new budget for the 21st year should be prepared and sent to the Headquarters for approval within half a month. The implementation of the new budget should begin on October 1st. Hereafter, any increase in expenses for various agencies should be prohibited in principle. If there are important and unavoidable matters, funds should be raised to offset them, so as not to repeat the old mistakes; (B) Raise new revenue to seek temporary reconciliation of income and expenditure. Bandit suppression work is related to the safety of the overall situation and is also the basis for reorganizing the province's various financial resources and construction projects. The total amount required each month is (1) Bandit suppression expenses for the troops stationed in Hubei are 226,540 yuan; (2) Special expenses are 93,000 yuan; (3) Military Commission bandit suppression expenses are 200,000 yuan; (4) The 21st Army's military expenses are 170,000 yuan; (5) Zhang Liansan's military expenses are 30,000 yuan. The total monthly amount is more than 640,000 yuan. Sufficient funding is needed for six months, totaling more than 3.8 million yuan. To raise this need, six measures have been approved: (1) Encourage the sale of public bonds, municipal public bonds, and aftercare public bonds. The unissued amount is more than 3.18 million yuan, which should be raised in the shortest possible time; (2) Sell official property and business. This refers to industries other than the official money bureau and public property. Large properties should be selected, such as the beach on Parrot Island and White Sand Island, and bid for sale; (3) Sell the Hanyang Iron and Steel Company steel rails detained by the province. The Ministry of Railways has previously sent personnel to Hubei to negotiate prices. The Headquarters should telegraph the Ministry of Railways to quickly negotiate prices and set payment in installments; (4) Clear Class A debt. The provincial government should invite representatives of Class A debt to discuss and modify the central old cases, local new cases, and the first and second programs, based on the situation. Negotiate the number of cash payments to meet urgent needs; (5) Collect rent. Hubei should follow Jiangsu's precedent and collect one month's rent in Hankou City for urgent use; (6) Recover the accounts from various counties. They should follow Zhejiang's urging method, post notices, and strictly urge settlement to emphasize public funds. The reorganization of regular income and expenditure measures mentioned in Item A and the reorganization of temporary income and expenditure measures mentioned in Item B should be handled by the provincial government, based on the actual situation, and reported for approval. In addition to distribution, this order should be followed." (September 3rd)

10th Division Recovers Huang'an County 60

Feng Xiuri and Environs See Three Days and Nights of Bloody Fighting

Nearly 10,000 Bandits Wounded or Killed, Dozens of Melee Battles

Bandits Flee to Deep Mountains After Li's Troops Enter the City

A correspondent from Hankou reports that after departing from Guangshui, the 10th Division under Li Mo'an advanced toward Huang'an, successively occupying Xiadian and Hekou. On August 10th, they arrived at Hekou Town and immediately supervised their troops to launch an attack on Huang'an City the next morning (11th). At 7:00 AM that morning, the vanguard made contact with the bandits near Dazhaojia and fought fiercely for several hours. The bandits were unable to withstand the attack and collapsed, fleeing toward the Dongyue Temple and Tongan Village. The 30th Brigade of the Li Division tracked and pursued them. After arriving near Dongyue Temple, they discovered that about 10,000 or more Red Bandits were stubbornly resisting in the fortresses of Guihualou, Liangtinggang, and Hejiajui, high ground. After the vanguard of the Li Division arrived, they occupied the high ground at the southern end of Dongyue Temple to cover the deployment of the main force, and used a portion to suppress the bandits in the area south of Guihualou, threatening their flanks. At this time, the fierce bloody battle in the Dongyue Temple area had gradually begun. At this moment of urgent artillery fire, Division Commander Li took the lead and personally went to the high ground west of Feng Xiuri to observe the position, supervise and direct, and occupy the vicinity of Dongyue Temple. Captured Red Bandits of the pseudo-11th Division confessed that the bandit units were the pseudo-10th, 11th, 12th, and 73rd divisions, and there was also the pseudo-Independent 1st Division and Independent Regiment that had rushed from Yinjiahe overnight last night. From this, it can be seen that the Red Bandits clearly wanted to concentrate their main force to break through one point to achieve their conspiracy of defeating each one separately. At this point, Li's Division changed its strategy and decided to consolidate its defense on the north-south line of the Feng Xiuri high ground, using fierce firepower to suppress the enemy and gathering forces on the left and right wings to prevent them from taking the opportunity to encircle them. At 3:00 PM, the bandits came more fiercely and launched a general offensive on the entire line, with the pseudo-11th Division encircling the left wing of Li's Division. After a fierce attack by Li's Division, they gradually collapsed. In this battle, more than 1,000 bandits were killed or wounded, and more than 100 were captured. Ni Zhiliang, the commander of the pseudo-11th Division, and Wu Yunshan, the regimental commander, were seriously injured. At about 4:00 PM, the 28th Brigade of Li's Division launched an attack on the left wing. After a fierce attack, the first and second lines of defense of the bandits were broken through by Li's Division. At that time, the right wing of the bandits had extended to the Luo Jiazhui line, and most of the bandits took the opportunity to encircle the rear of the left wing of Li's Division. A regiment of the General Reserve Team of Li's Division and the units directly under the division immediately reinforced, engaging in melee battles dozens of times, and finally annihilating all the bandits without a single survivor. By this time, dusk had arrived, and Li's Division added fortifications to the original positions and maintained strict vigilance. It can be seen that they were brave and good at fighting to deal with five divisions of the enemy with one division.

On the 12th, the main line had been temporarily calm. At noon, when it rained heavily, a part of the bandits came to attack. They collapsed after being met by the left-wing troops of Li's Division. At 3:00 PM, most of the bandits suddenly moved to the left. At 4:00 PM, more than a dozen mounted pseudo-military officers led dozens of bandits to reconnaissance in front of the right-wing position of Li's Division. They were shot down by Li's Division with machine guns. Dai, the commander of the pseudo-Independent 1st Division, was also shot and killed near Li Chenglu. The bandits' repeated offensives were fiercely attacked by Li's Division, causing many casualties. At this time, the 83rd and 89th Divisions had gradually spread out on the left and right wings of Li's Division, and the Second Column had advanced to Qiliping. The bandits themselves were under greater threat.

At dawn on the 13th, Li's Division, seeing that the time was ripe, launched a large-scale attack on Huang'an. After fighting the bandits again in the Liangtinggang Tianma Temple area, they drove straight in. At 3:00 PM, they completely occupied Huang'an County. The remnant bandits were extremely embarrassed and fled to the mountains in the northeast. According to the people of Huang'an, the bandits suffered nearly 10,000 casualties in this battle and have completely collapsed.

Central Political Council Passes Principles of Statistics Law 61

Central Political Council passed nine principles of the Statistics Law, as amended, at its 323rd meeting on August 31st, and has sent them to the Legislative Yuan for drafting a Statistics Law. The principles are recorded as follows: (1) Statistics that should be handled by the government shall be handled separately by the relevant agencies with direct relationship; (2) The following statistics shall be handled by the Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government: (1) Those belonging to the national basic census; (2) Those that should not belong exclusively to the scope of any agency; (3) Those that the agencies have not been able to investigate and compile; (3) Governments at all levels may handle local statistics within the scope of statistics of the upper-level government without conflict; (4) The records and registers of public officials and their work in various agencies shall be managed by statistical personnel; (5) The legislative, judicial, examination, and supervisory agencies may, in order to exercise their powers, discuss with the highest accounting agency and order the statistical personnel of the various agencies to handle the special statistics they need; (6) The division of the scope of statistical affairs and other matters that should be neatly and uniformly divided shall be decided by the National Accounting Conference; (7) The degree of openness of statistics handled by the government shall be divided into three categories: (1) Secret category, which shall not be disclosed; (2) Open category, which can be disclosed but should be kept secret under certain conditions, shall still be regarded as a secret category under those conditions; (3) Public announcement category, which must be announced under the prescribed conditions; (8) Those who are investigated when the government handles statistics, whether they are agencies or individuals, have the obligation to report truthfully and in detail; (9) The government and its personnel shall not, when handling statistics, use their powers and positions to hinder the rights of those who are investigated.

Legislative Yuan Passes Silk Industry Public Bond Regulations 62

Exclusively for Relieving the Silk Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

The Legislative Yuan held its 200th meeting on the morning of the 3rd and passed the 14 articles of the Public Bond Regulations for the Short-Term Silk Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang in the 21st year of the Republic of China. The full text is as follows: Article 1: This public bond shall be issued by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and named the Short-Term Silk Industry Public Bond of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in the 21st year of the Republic of China. Article 2: The fixed amount of this public bond is 3 million yuan. Article 3: The use of this public bond is exclusively for relieving the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Article 4: The annual interest rate of this public bond is set at 7%. Article 5: This public bond is scheduled to be issued on October 1, 21st year of the Republic of China. Article 6: This public bond shall be issued at 100% of its face value. Article 7: Starting from October 21st year of the Republic of China, the interest payment dates for this public bond shall be March 31, June 30, September 30, and December 31 each year. Article 8: The first principal repayment date for this public bond is December 31, 21st year of the Republic of China. Subsequently, the principal shall be repaid once every three months, with an average repayment of one-sixteenth each time, and a repayment of one-quarter each year. The interest shall be reduced with the principal, and the principal and interest shall be fully repaid by the end of September 25th year of the Republic of China. The repayment of the bond shall be determined by lottery. The aforementioned lottery shall be conducted at the Shanghai Banking Association on March 15, June 15, September 15, and December 15 each year. During the lottery, one person each shall be dispatched by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and the auditing agencies, and one representative each shall be dispatched by the Shanghai Banking Association and the Jiangsu and Zhejiang silk and cocoon industries to jointly supervise. Article 9: The principal and interest fund payable for this public bond shall be designated from the allocation of the abolition of likin to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces by the Ministry of Finance. Every three months, the amount payable according to the principal and interest repayment schedule of this public bond shall be transferred by the Ministry of Finance to the National Goods Bank for payment to the fund management committee of this public bond for the purpose of payment of principal and interest when due, until the repayment is completed and shall not be changed. Article 10: The principal and interest payment matters of this public bond shall be handled by the Fund Management Committee, and the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the China Industrial Bank, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Local Industrial Bank, and the Jiangsu Bank shall be designated as the principal and interest payment agencies. Article 11: The face value of this public bond is divided into two types: 1,000 yuan and 100 yuan, both of which are bearer bonds. Article 12: This public bond may be freely mortgaged and traded. If Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces need to pay a deposit for official business, it may be used as collateral. Article 13: Anyone who forges this public bond or damages its credit shall be punished by the judicial authorities in accordance with the law. Article 14: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation.

Hai River Regulation Project Nearing Completion 63

The Hai River Commission's Dismantlement Still Problematic

Tianjin Correspondence: The Hai River in this city is the confluence of the five major rivers: the North Canal, Ziya River, Daqing River, South Canal, and Yongding River. Before 1926, the river flowed smoothly, and merchant ships with drafts of 15 or 16 feet could pass unimpeded year-round. Unexpectedly, during the flood season of 1927, the Yongding River experienced a flash flood, carrying silt and sediment downstream, causing the Hai River to silt up by seven or eight feet. Merchant ships with drafts of over ten feet could not reach Tianjin Port without waiting for high tide. This drew the attention of the city's residents at the time. Subsequently, the silting worsened year by year, further alarming people both domestically and internationally. The city originally had a Hai River Engineering Bureau, with annual expenditures of 1.5 to 1.6 million yuan, established according to the Boxer Protocol. Consuls from Britain, America, France, and Japan served as directors of the bureau, with significant power held by foreigners. Despite the large annual expenditures, they failed to earnestly dredge the Hai River. In 1928, when Shang Zhen was Chairman of Hebei Province, he listed the regulation of the Hai River as

one of the major construction policies. He then gathered experts to study both temporary and

Page 10

permanent solutions. The permanent solution required no less than 20 million yuan, but due to difficulties in raising funds at the time, it could not be implemented. The temporary solution only required four to five million yuan, which involved diverting the silt and sediment from the Yongding River elsewhere and then introducing clean water into the Hai River. Its effective period was estimated to be about 20 years. Therefore, the Hai River Regulation Commission was established, issuing five million yuan in Hai River regulation public bonds, secured by a 25% surtax on Tianjin Customs duties

for principal and interest repayment. The central government approved the issuance of four million yuan, with an estimated completion time of 18 months. Unexpectedly, the overall situation was turbulent, and construction only began in 1930. Water release gates, control gates, and ship locks were built near Beicang, and only completed in May of this year. On July 1st, the gates were opened to release the silt, with the Taha River Depression serving as the silt disposal area, covering an area of approximately 250,000 mu. This silt disposal area was mostly alkaline land, unsuitable for planting grains, because the northern water retaining dikes had not yet been constructed. By August, the released floodwaters had overflowed beyond the silt disposal area, so the gates were closed. However, the Yongding River's floodwaters, carrying silt and sediment, still flowed into the Hai River, causing silting as before. Several years of regulation, costing millions of yuan, achieved only this result. Currently, the commission still has a remaining balance of less than one million yuan, which will be used to excavate a water diversion river to bring clean water into the Hai River and to purchase private land in the silt disposal area. It is estimated that by May of next year, the funds will be exhausted, and the regulation project will be completed. During the period before the completion of this project, there are still tens of thousands of yuan in remaining funds. A group of students who have returned from overseas see this and some people are proposing to save money and merge with the North China Water Conservancy Commission. However, the Hai River Regulation Commission, with the provincial chairman and mayor as chairman and vice-chairman, and the Tianjin Customs Superintendent and Construction Bureau Director as ex-officio members, each receiving monthly transportation stipends of 300 to 500 yuan, naturally opposes the merger. Recently, with a change in the provincial chairman, the Ministries of Interior and Foreign Affairs dispatched Sun Shifu and Chen Haichao to Tianjin to, together with Han Linsheng, the Tianjin Customs Superintendent designated by the Ministry of Finance, handle the merger. After Chen and Sun arrived in Tianjin, they contacted Han Linsheng several times. Since the provincial chairman, Yu Xuezhong, had not yet taken office, the commission's Secretary-General, Huang Zongfa, was only assisting and had no desire to cling to his position, but could not make a decision on the merger issue without a full meeting.

for resolution.

According to the observations of the general public, the commission's merger may still be problematic. The reason given by the receiving side is that since the September 18th Incident, financial difficulties have been severe, and the entire country is implementing austerity policies. The Hai River Regulation Commission's temporary solution project is 90% complete, so why waste public funds further? It should be merged with the North China Water Conservancy Commission to save expenses. The reason given by the Hai River Commission for opposing the merger is that the North China Water Conservancy Commission is a design organization, not an implementing organization. It received the Shunzhi Water Conservancy Commission a few years ago, and in the years since, besides publishing weather reports in the Ta Kung Pao every day, it has hardly done any work. The Hai River Commission built water gates in Beicang to block floodwaters and introduce clean water, preventing the Hai River from silting up year by year, to facilitate the traffic of merchant ships on the Hai River. Furthermore, the alkaline land in the silt disposal area, covering approximately 250,000 mu, is currently only worth one yuan per mu. After this silt disposal, in three to five years, it will become fertile land, worth ten to twenty yuan per mu. This is a significant achievement that benefits farmers and transportation. Moreover, the Hai River Engineering Bureau spends one hundred and several tens of thousands of yuan annually, with only a few dredging boats as window dressing, resembling a retirement home for foreigners. During the workers' strike this spring, one of the demands pointed out the disparity in treatment, stating that the foreman (i.e., night watchman) in the Engineering Bureau was a Westerner, with a monthly salary of 160 taels, while the Chinese foreman and servants only received ten or so yuan per month. From this one example, other aspects can be imagined. The Hai River Regulation Commission intends to take over the Hai River Engineering Bureau after completing the temporary solution project, because the Hai River Regulation Commission is the direct agency for governing the Hai River, and the Hai River Engineering Bureau's work is ineffective, so it should be handed over to the Hai River Commission. If the Hai River Commission is merged into the Water Conservancy Commission now, it is feared that there will be no courage to take back the Hai River Engineering Bureau. (September 2nd)

Jiangsu Province's Plan to Reorganize All Provincial Land 64

Zhao Qilu Has Drafted Two Plans

Yesterday Went to the Provincial Land Bureau to Take Over and Inspect

Zhenjiang Correspondence: Jiangsu's land administration previously had a Land Reorganization Committee, headed by Chen Hexian. It was later changed to the Provincial Land Bureau, with Zhu Wenxin as the director. During this period of political tutelage, land administration is extremely important. It is insufficient to direct smoothly without raising the director's authority. Therefore, at the Provincial Government's 524th meeting, Chairman Gu proposed that the director of the Provincial Land Bureau be concurrently held by the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs. After Director Zhao Qilu of the Department of Civil Affairs received the order, he drafted two plans for the overall reorganization of Jiangsu's land, a three-year plan and a five-year plan, both extremely complete. The three-year plan has a shorter timeframe, but requires more surveying instruments and talent cultivation. The five-year plan requires slightly fewer instruments and talent, but has a longer timeframe. The total expenditure is budgeted to be between 30 and 50 million yuan. The provincial government believes this matter is of great importance and has assigned the directors of the Departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, and Construction to jointly review it, so that the overall land policy will advance to a more perfect state. Zhao also advocated simultaneously raising the authority of the county bureaus. Therefore, at the Provincial Government's 525th meeting, a proposal was also passed for the county magistrates of Zhenjiang, Jiangning, and Qingpu to concurrently serve as directors of the land bureau. The internal organization of the Provincial Land Bureau itself is also striving to be strengthened. It is heard that a secretary will be added to assist in management. Zhao already went yesterday (September 2nd) to take over and gathered staff for a sincere speech. The review of the entire reorganization plan will be completed in the shortest possible time. Details will be explored and published subsequently.

Overview of Yijun 66

Yijun County's county seat uses the high mountains as a natural barrier on one side. The county government is built here, overlooking the entire county and being the best location. Most residents live at the foot of the mountains. The county's area is about 300 li from east to west and about 120 li from north to south. Cultivated land accounts for two-thirds of the county, and wasteland accounts for one-third. Tax revenue is about 7,000 yuan per year. The county's population is about 50,000 people. The county seat has about 200 households and over 600 people. The county seat only has Changshi Street, where stalls gather, and the situation is still quite lively.

The county has more than 30 primary schools, one higher primary school. The county seat also has a model primary school and a girls' primary school. The county's primary school students are about 300 to 400 people, and higher primary school has about 80 to 90 people. Education funding is about 5,000 yuan per year. Tuition is not collected. Teacher salaries are about 70 to 80 yuan per year for primary school, and the higher primary school's principal is 240 yuan per year and teachers are 200 yuan. (Sent from Yijun on the morning of the 22nd)

Local Correspondence

Taicang 67

The Zhu Case's Situation Is Becoming Increasingly Serious. Zhu Tieying, the editor of the Moye Daily, angered the county government by reporting on business taxes, resulting in a prison sentence and the closure of the newspaper. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that business leaders and local gentry have repeatedly requested County Magistrate Zhao in person to allow bail, but all requests have been denied. They then retreated to request that the judgment be sent out as soon as possible so that the defendant can appeal, but this was also rejected. He even said to detain him for ten or so days before talking. If local tabloids publish unfavorable news in the future, they will all be severely punished without leniency. This has caused merchants and residents throughout the county to feel indignant, saying that freedom of speech has been clearly stated by Premier Wang, and what the Moye Daily reported was also based on facts and was not inciting merchants to resist taxes. Whether Zhu's guilt is justified is another matter, but the newspaper was imprisoned for speaking out for the merchants, so the merchants should help him. Therefore, Zhu and others have been adding seals to various businesses for days, unanimously requesting bail. If this does not achieve the purpose, they are willing to sacrifice everything and make further demands. The situation is very serious.

Robbers of the Dade Ship Executed by Firing Squad. Last autumn, after the Dade Jiang ship of the Shanghai-Yangzhou route of the Dada Company was robbed at Liuxu Port in Jingjiang, Huang Bingzhong, the detective chief of the Su-Chang Command, captured a robber named Yan Linlin in Taohuagang in the Western District. Wuxi 69

Autumn Cocoon Market Opens on the 7th. The local Cocoon Industry Guild believes that the autumn fresh cocoons are about to enter the market, and the cocoon price and opening date should be discussed in advance to avoid temporary hesitation. Therefore, at 3 PM on the previous day (the 3rd), a general meeting of all members was held at the guild hall in Xujianong. Over 180 people attended, including Jiang Daoshan, Wu Shimei, Huang Zhuoru, Hua Zicai, Yang Mengqian, Gu Binsheng, and Gao Shufang. Hua Shaochun chaired the meeting. (1) He reported that "Our industry has been extremely declining in recent years, and last year's autumn cocoons saw fierce competition among various merchants, causing great pain. If we want to turn things around, we hope that fellow merchants will unite and jointly seek ways to revive Jiangsu." Regarding the taxes and levies that the cocoon industry should pay, the guild repeatedly requested exemptions during the spring cocoon season. The business tax on all cocoon merchants was approved for a one-year suspension, and the cocoon stove business tax collected by the Construction Bureau was also approved for suspension. The house tax for cocoon merchants was also approved for exemption. However, now that the autumn cocoon season is approaching, some collection agencies still have documents intending to collect taxes, which the guild has politely refused. (2) Discussed the price of this year's autumn cocoons and decided that the standard price for each dan of autumn fresh cocoons should be 40 yuan in silver dollars, with higher prices for better quality and lower prices for poorer quality. (3) Discussed the opening date of this year's autumn cocoon market and decided to set it for September 7th. Those who wish to delay are allowed to do so. The meeting adjourned.

Shop Owner's Wife Commits Suicide After Being Abused by Husband. Xin Xin Shop owner Wei Daosheng hanged himself under the Taiding Bridge in the county seat. Originally from Danyang, he married a woman named Leng and lived together in the shop. However, the shop's business was slow, and the economy was difficult. Wei was obsessed with gambling and indulged in it all day. The day before, Wei was gambling at a neighbor's house, and his wife Leng found out. When Wei returned home, they immediately had an argument, and Wei abused Leng. Out of anger, Leng went to the attic and hanged herself. When Wei Daosheng discovered it, she was already dead.

Zhenjiang 71

Jiangsu Province Establishes a Radio Station. The Jiangsu Provincial Government, due to the rampant banditry in Jiangbei, has established a radio station and four branch stations to maintain communication with major ports such as Nanjing and Shanghai. The main station is the former radio station of the Construction Bureau, which was allocated to the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The branch stations are the four that were temporarily established in Yangzhou, Gaoyou, and Qingjiang. It is now deemed necessary to establish formal radio stations permanently. Nanjing has also established a station. In addition, it can communicate with Jinan, Hangzhou, Ji'an, Beiping, and Hankou. The director of the main station was previously concurrently held as a voluntary position by a technician of the Construction Bureau. The foreman of the station is Dai Yuzao, who has held the position for three years and has also planned the affairs of the branch stations. Now that it is under the management of the provincial government, Dai is expected to be promoted to director. The monthly expenses of the main station are 435 yuan, and its staffing is 120 yuan for the director and foreman, 80 to 70 yuan for telegraphers, and 60 to 40 yuan for clerks. If another foreman is established, it would be 100 to 90 yuan. The rest are electricity, gasoline, and miscellaneous expenses. The Nanjing radio station is established at the embassy residence, and the director is Shen Weijia. The monthly expenses are 438 yuan, and its staffing is the same as the main station. It is heard that the director of the Beijing station has already received the generator and is expected to start telegraphing soon.

Nantong 72

County Government Executes Bandit Leader in the Eastern Countryside. Zhang Linlin, the bandit leader in the eastern countryside of Tong County, has been gathering crowds to rob and kill for over ten years. He was captured by the Public Security Bureau last month in Tianshenggang and sent to the county government for interrogation. He confessed without denial and was sentenced to death. The provincial government approved the sentence on the 3rd and was immediately escorted to the execution ground east of the city for execution by firing squad.

County Surtax Collateral Loan Bond Issuance Postponed. Tong County, in order to alleviate the local financial situation, has agreed to issue 100,000 yuan of county surtax collateral loan bonds. Now that the land price tax has been levied, the county government meeting decided to postpone the issuance.

Change of Commander of the Fourth District of the Water Police. Jiang Chaosong, the commander of the Fourth District of the Provincial Water Police, was dismissed and replaced by Zhang Xianyi. On the 3rd, the Department of Civil Affairs ordered County Magistrate Zhang Dong to supervise Zhang District Commander's assumption of office and appointed Wang Guoliang and Hu Dingfen as chiefs of the First and Second Sections, and Tao Fengwei as the captain of the offshore patrol team.

Gaoyou 73

Bandits From Bao Ying Apprehended in You. The county police team previously received a letter from the Bao Ying County Government stating that the dangerous bandits Chen Changyuan and others had repeatedly committed serious crimes in our county and are now hiding in Dujia Alley, Wangying Town, your county. Please send a team to arrest them. Team Leader Zhu immediately dispatched a team led by the deputy team leader. The dangerous bandit Chen Changyuan was arrested, and three small hostages were rescued. The hostages were handed over to the Bao Ying Self-Defense Corps to take away. Chen was escorted to the city, but when he reached the Miaoxiangkou outside the North Gate, he happened to run into Chen's accomplice Wang Guisheng (i.e., Wang Laohan), so Wang was also taken into custody. After Team Leader Zhu briefly interrogated them, they were transferred to the county government for interrogation today (the 2nd).

Jiangsu Province's Opium Monopoly Implemented. The opium monopoly has been rumored for a long time. When the rumors were at their peak last month, it seemed that it would be realized immediately. Later, due to strong opposition from public opinion, the atmosphere gradually became quiet. Now, according to a friend's letter from Zhenjiang, the Opium Monopoly Bureau has rented a house on the riverside in Zhenjiang to work. A large batch of government opium has been shipped to Zhenjiang on the 22nd

and is scheduled to be implemented from September 1st. As for the organization of the monopoly agency, under the General Bureau, the 61 counties in the province are divided into 15 districts, each with a special office, and each office governs four to six counties. Each county has a monopoly sub-bureau. The monopoly method is completely different from the method of recruiting contractors when the monopoly was implemented in 1928. It is heard that a three-month trial period will be temporarily used. During the trial period, all offices and bureaus will uniformly recruit contractors. In addition to necessary expenses, the actual sales will be settled. After the trial period expires, the results will be assessed to determine the method. As for the contractors, the provincial General Bureau is managed by a Mr. Lu, and the remaining offices and bureaus have been contracted by Mr. Lu separately. The internal organization of the provincial General Bureau and each special office bureau are uniformly divided into three sections, with the first section in charge of general affairs, the second section in charge of operations, and the third section in charge of auditing. It is also heard that the director of the Gaoyou Sub-bureau is a Mr. Cheng.

Huzhou 74

Bandits Robbing on the Road. Shen Acai, a farmer from the Guoxiawan area in the southwestern countryside of Huzhou, came to the city on the 1st of this month and sold 23 silver dollars of silk. After purchasing cloth and miscellaneous goods, he had 18 silver dollars left. When Acai was returning home that day, he encountered three bandits dressed in short clothes and speaking with a Henan accent on the main road at the crossroads. They stopped him and claimed to be searching for opium. As Acai was about to shout, one bandit took out a pistol and snatched his basket of miscellaneous goods, dragging him into the woods and robbing him of all the silver dollars he was carrying.

Ningbo 75

Change of Director of the Water Police Bureau. Wang Wenhan, the director of the Zhenhai Water Police Bureau, has been in office for more than three years. Due to insufficient funding and difficulties in handling affairs, he has repeatedly requested his resignation from the provincial government. The provincial government, seeing his firm intention to resign, has already approved it and appointed Ouyang Ge to replace him. It is heard that Ge will come to take office soon.

It was completed a long time ago and is temporarily managed by the Yin County Government. The director has already arrived in Yong from Shanghai yesterday with clerks and other personnel. After finding suitable office space, they will take office and start work soon.

Education News Highlights

Petitions from Elementary Education Circles Across Various Regions to the Ministry of Education to Improve Elementary School Textbooks 76

Restricting Book Merchants' Monopoly

Rewarding Private Authorship

Representatives from elementary education circles in Beijing, Shanghai, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other places, including Chen Heqin, Shi Renfu, Jiang Xicen, and Yi Kexun, totaling several dozen people, jointly submitted a petition to the Ministry of Education yesterday (the 2nd), requesting rewards for private authorship and restrictions on the monopoly of book merchants, in order to improve elementary school textbooks and illustrations. The original petition stated: "Upon investigation, elementary school textbooks and illustrations in European and American countries mostly adopt a free review system. The main reason for this is to allow private individuals to freely compete, so that they can continuously improve and excellent versions can emerge repeatedly. Since China has had textbooks, it has also adopted this system. However, while the name allows private competition, in reality, two or three shrewd book merchants manipulate and monopolize, leaving no room for freedom. These two or three book merchants believe that elementary school textbooks and illustrations have a very wide market and are therefore a major source of profit. Thus, when editing, they employ penniless writers at extremely low wages, directing their work and setting time limits, only seeking to copy old versions and quickly produce books, disregarding the needs of the times and the psychology of children, and lacking any ideal or purpose. When printing, the illustrations are simple and crude, colors are completely absent, the text is kept short, and the paper is reduced as much as possible, in order to minimize costs and maximize profits. For distribution, they widely establish salespersons, bribe those in the education circles, and engage in various activities, using all means to expand sales, regardless of the methods used. Therefore, although their products have many titles, the content remains unchanged, repeating old patterns until the present day. There is no shortage of individuals in the education circles who are knowledgeable, experienced, and capable of writing better elementary school textbooks and illustrations. However, when they sell their manuscripts, the book merchants are sure to suppress the price, so that they gain little despite exhausting their efforts. When it comes to taxation, the book merchants turn a blind eye, and they cannot find patrons everywhere they look. If they print themselves, they lack both capital and distribution channels, making it absolutely impossible to compete with the book merchants. Even if there are one or two small book merchants willing to pay royalties and undertake the printing of their works, they are inevitably swallowed up by trusts due to their limited funds and weak strength. Therefore, even those with ambition hesitate and turn back, not daring to try. Because the book merchants manipulate and monopolize at the top, and private individuals hesitate and turn back at the bottom, there is no hope for improvement in China's elementary school textbooks and illustrations. The damage this causes to education is truly beyond words. We have heard that the central government, due to the poor quality of elementary school textbooks and illustrations, has considered hiring experts to edit them themselves. This would certainly correct the abuses of the book merchants' monopoly. However, this matter is of great importance and is not easy to accomplish. This is because the writing and editing of elementary school textbooks and illustrations requires an objective attitude and the use of scientific methods. The creation of each word and sentence often requires exhausting one's efforts. Even composing old poems is not as easy as writing textbooks and illustrations for middle school and above, and it is even less like writing papers or novels, where one can write thousands of words with ease. Therefore, the government will find it difficult to find experts to recruit, and the costs will be enormous, and the completion of the books will be difficult. This is all within expectations. We believe that the simplest way to improve elementary school textbooks and illustrations is to adopt a free review system, on the one hand rewarding private authorship and on the other hand restricting the monopoly of book merchants. We humbly present the following specific methods: 1. The Ministry should issue clear commendations or provide bonuses for outstanding and innovative elementary school textbooks and illustrations after they have been reviewed and approved, in order to show encouragement. 2. If excellent books are published by book merchants and the author receives royalties, the Ministry may, after review and approval, instruct the education administrative organs of various provinces and cities to order the elementary schools under their jurisdiction to give priority to adopting them. 3. Stipulate that the principle for the creation of elementary school textbooks and illustrations should be royalty payments, and the Ministry should order all book merchants to comply. 4. The Ministry should order the education administrative organs of various provinces and cities to instruct elementary school education administrators and school faculty and staff not to accept subsidies or preferential treatment from book merchants, except in cases where they have a publishing relationship with the book merchants. Those who accept subsidies and lobby for sales on behalf of the book merchants will be immediately dismissed upon discovery, and those whose circumstances are more serious will be prosecuted for bribery. If both reward and restriction are taken into account, the effect of private competition can be seen, and there will be no worry that elementary school textbooks and illustrations will not be continuously improved and excellent versions will emerge repeatedly. The central government can also sit back and watch the improvement of textbooks and illustrations, without having to consider self-editing. We are either elementary school teachers who secretly hope for textbook improvements, or have served as authors, understanding the malpractices involved. Therefore, we dare to comprehensively present our views, respectfully requesting review, approval, and implementation. The future of elementary school education truly depends on it." It is reported that the Ministry of Education will consider adopting the petition after receiving it.

Jiangsu Education Department Orders to Raise the Level of Middle Schools (1) 77

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to forward the plan to raise the level of middle schools for compliance and strict implementation. The order to the county education bureaus states: "Since the director of this department took office, he has formulated the policy guidelines for the second half of the 20th year of the department, and the fourth item in the improvement of provincial and county education is 'effectively raising the level of ordinary middle schools.' Subsequently, the Jiangsu Education Three-Year Plan was formulated, and the eighth item in the phased implementation is 'reorganizing ordinary middle schools.' However, the former plan only listed the outline and did not specify detailed methods. Now, a plan to raise the level of middle schools has been formulated, and the principles and methods have been listed separately, which can serve as a standard for implementation. However, it has been found that the teaching of each subject in each school often fails to predetermine a plan of action, and the selection of materials for the Chinese language subject is particularly lacking in standards, resulting in a failure to see increased effectiveness. It is especially important to formulate a teaching plan for each subject in accordance with the aforementioned plan within one month after the document is received, and submit it for review. In addition to distributing it separately, the aforementioned plan is printed and distributed, ordering the directors of the bureaus to forward it to all public and private middle schools under their jurisdiction for compliance and strict implementation. This order."

Plan to Raise the Level of Middle Schools (Passed by the Tenth Departmental Meeting on August 26, 21st Year)

The curriculum of middle schools in this province varies, and the content is not substantial enough, resulting in uneven student levels and inadequate academic abilities. In order to seek balanced progress, there must be a unified plan. The plan formulated by this department is as follows: Center of the plan to raise the level of middle schools: The proposed plan is as follows: A. Principles: 1. Implement the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry. 2. Carefully select excellent teachers. 3. Enhance teaching effectiveness. 4. Encourage extracurricular activities. 5. Strictly examine academic performance. 6. Enrich school facilities. B. Methods: First, Regarding administration: (1) Provincial Education Administration: 1. Order all middle schools to implement the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry, and supplement them with reference to special needs. 2. Formulate minimum equipment standards for each subject in each school, examine the actual situation, and gradually enrich them within the scope of economic possibility. 3. Formulate detailed rules for the service of faculty and staff. 4. Order all principals to report the actual service of faculty and staff on a monthly basis for evaluation. 5. Strictly examine the weekly class hours, the number of class days per semester, and the implementation of teaching methods for each subject in each school. 6. Urge teachers to engage in research on teaching methods and curriculum materials. 7. Implement middle school graduation examinations, and comment on the quality of student performance as one of the criteria for evaluating principals. 8. Hold provincial or regional subject competitions and exhibitions, and various competitive activities such as essay writing and speech contests for each subject. (2) School Administration: 1. Promote the system of full-time teachers, and make long-term employment a principle. 2. Teachers who teach required courses should be promoted with their original classes, so that they are fully responsible for the courses they teach. 3. Each school should implement ability grouping within the possible scope according to the nature of the subjects. Students with lower ability in each subject should be instructed by the teachers in charge during spare time or holidays, and effectively tutored. 4. The principal and the director of studies or the director of instruction should assess the teachers' teaching materials, teaching methods, and the diligence of grading homework. 5. Organize various research societies for teachers and students. 6. Encourage teachers and students to publish papers on academic research. 7. Hold literary and academic competitions, speech competitions, and exhibitions every semester. 8. Exchange teachers for lectures in each school. 9. Invite more academic experts to give lectures at the school. 10. Equipment for each subject should be enriched as much as possible in accordance with equipment standards. 11. Hold more temporary oral examinations, written examinations, and regular tests within a semester. 12. Examination grading should formulate concrete standards separately according to the content of each subject. 13. At the end of the academic year, students of each grade should be guided to use the holidays to make a comprehensive review of the subjects learned in the academic year, and hold a review examination in the first week of the next academic year. (To be continued)

Meeting of the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council 78

The 11th Council Meeting of the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council of China was held at 3:00 PM on September 4th. Attendees included Tong Xingbai, Wang Gang, Yu Kuaiyuan, Leng Xueqiao, and Zhao Weizu. Wang Gang chaired the meeting, and Luo Lie served as the recorder. 1. Formal salutation. 2. Report Items: (1) Chairman's report on the past state of council affairs. (2) Report from the General Affairs Section on the financial situation of the council from January to August. (3) Council member Xu Peihuang resigned from his position in the Education Bureau and requested permission to resign from his position as council member. (4) Report from the Compilation Section on past work. 3. Discussion Items: (1) Whether the council's staff should be re-hired. Resolved: All existing paid staff will be dismissed, each receiving one month's salary as severance pay, and Luo Lie will be hired as secretary, and Zhou Ming will be hired as a resident staff member. (2) Council member Leng proposed how to reorganize Boy Scout training in the city after the war. Resolved: To be handled by the Assessment Section in conjunction with the Compilation and Guidance Sections. (3) Council member Leng proposed how to reorganize Boy Scout uniforms in the city. Resolved: To be planned and handled by the Guidance Section. (4) The council members of this term have long been expired, and instructions have been requested from the Command Headquarters, but have not yet been approved. How should this be handled? Resolved: To be submitted to the Preparatory Office of the General Council. (5) Council member Qu and Secretary Luo advanced the second motion of the second meeting of the eighth council meeting, which was submitted to draft a plan for the fourth grand review and grand camping of the city's Boy Scouts. Now that the plan has been drafted, please revise and implement it. Resolved: To be handed over to the Standing Council members. (6) Boy Scouts who participated in wartime health work should be commended. Resolved: Each will be awarded a certificate of merit. (7) Council member Leng proposed that the Moore Memorial Church and the Postal Workers' Union Boy Scout troops worked hardest in the past in the Wartime Service Corps and should be specially rewarded. Resolved: Each will be awarded a banner, and each of the other troops will be awarded a certificate of merit. (8) Please determine the date of the council's regular meetings in the future. Resolved: Once every two weeks, on Saturdays at 2:00 PM. (9) Council member Xu Peihuang's letter requesting resignation. Resolved: A letter will be sent to the new Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Mr. Pan Gongzhan, to take over.

National Mandarin Promotion Association's Sixth Anniversary Celebration 79

The National Mandarin Education Promotion Association held its sixth anniversary celebration at 8:45 AM on the first day of this month at the Shanghai Asia-America Company Radio Station. After the ceremony, Jian Shikeng reported on the association's affairs: (5) preparing a Shanghai members' get-together; (6) preparing a Mandarin language and arts children's competition; (7) the face-to-face teaching department of the Mandarin language training session will open courses in phonetic symbols and Mandarin speaking; the correspondence department will open a course in phonetic symbols, using phonograph records and lectures to teach; (8) the association will implement the resolutions of last year's National Mandarin Education Discussion Conference, requesting the competent authorities to notify all film companies nationwide that, starting on January 1, 1933, all newly released silent films must add a phonetic symbol table before the film, and the subtitles in the film must be in Mandarin and include phonetic symbols. Newly released sound films must have the phonetic symbols read aloud before the film or have a phonetic symbol song sung, with subtitles for comparison. The dialogue and subtitles in the film must be in Mandarin, otherwise they will not be approved. Old films must also be modified in accordance with the order and resubmitted for approval, otherwise they will not be allowed to be screened. The competent authorities are also requested to notify agencies across the country to comply. After the report was completed, Ms. Ren Ning, a student from Shanghai Middle School Experimental Elementary School, sang "Let's Go to the Battlefield," and Ms. Fang Ruzhen, Qian Xiujuan, Zhu Xiuqi, and Wu Gangmin, students from Wuben Girls' Middle School Attached Elementary School, sang "Ants Love to Work." Finally, there were phonetic symbol songs, folk songs, nursery rhymes, and other performances from Beijing, Guangzhou, Suzhou, and other places. The meeting adjourned at 9:40 AM.

Lingnan Army Narrowly Lost in Tennis Match The match started at 2:00 PM at the China Tennis Court. Volleyball Match: No Result A volleyball match was played against Yinghua at the China Athletic Field. According to the rules, the winner was determined by the best of five sets, but the match was stopped after the third set. The score was 21-18, 21-14, 14-21, with the 20th Army in the lead. A dispute then arose. Because the reporter was at the tennis court, he did not know the truth. The staff of the Coordination Association were also at the tennis court, so they also did not know what happened. Afterwards, both teams were asked, and the reasons obtained were as follows: (1) The Yinghua team said that it had been agreed in advance that the winner would be determined by the best of five sets, but after the third set, the 20th Army players all left the field and did not continue the match. The referee could not call them back and there was no way to play. (2) The 20th Army team said that when the third set ended, the referee announced that our team had won, so our team believed that the match was over and left the field. If our team had left the field without reason, the referee could have announced that our team had forfeited. The referee did not announce that our team had forfeited, so our team actually followed the referee's decision and did not leave the field without reason. Afterwards, the Coordination Association looked for the referee to resolve the issue, but the referee had left, so the doubt could not be resolved. In short, the spirit of the game is the most important thing, and victory or defeat is secondary.

Lingnan Defeated Qinghua in the Last Two Minutes 86

A Ratio of Three to Two

An Important Scene in the Summer Soccer League

In the Summer Soccer League, there was an important match yesterday. Lingnan and Qinghua had never encountered opponents in Part 1. Yesterday they met at the China Baseball Field. As a result, Lingnan scored a goal against Qinghua in the last two minutes and won 3-2. The referee was Jiang Xiangqing.

Lingnan Scored Two Goals First Qinghua's sharp forwards attacked several times, once from the left and twice from the right, with excellent opportunities, but they failed due to inaccurate shooting. Lingnan's strong defensive line, Chen Jiaqiu and Feng Yunyou, two great pillars, closely monitored them. Then, progressing to the front of Qinghua's goal, Zhu Zhicheng kicked a corner kick, which landed in front of the goal. Chen Hongguang shot it into the net. Afterwards, although both sides had fierce attacks, they were ineffective. Chen Jiaqiu had two long-range shots from 30 yards from the goal, which were rapid and fierce, but were unfortunately saved by the goalkeeper. In the second half, Qinghua still had fierce attacks, but after ten minutes, Lingnan's left winger, Zhu Zhicheng, went straight in and quickly passed to Chen Hongguang, who sent it to the right. The right winger, Tang Wenwei, sent it in, and the score was 2-0, and the situation seemed set.

Qinghua Returned to a Tie But in the ten minutes near the end, the situation changed dramatically. Qinghua scored two goals in five minutes, creating a tie. First, center-back Ye Jinjin intercepted the ball and sent it to right winger Cao Qiuting. Cao was an outstanding player in Qinghua yesterday, with swift steps. Even Chen Jiaqiu tried his best to monitor him. He is a talent that can be developed, but his position is not yet accurate and needs to be trained. Cao then sent the ball to the center, and center forward Shao Jihua scored. Soon after, the leader came again, and Cao Guorong shot in from the left, and the bad situation suddenly turned into a peaceful situation. The Last Two Minutes Spring clouds were initially displayed, and the changes were infinite. Although there were only two minutes left, the outcome was determined in this period. Lingnan was in an extremely advantageous position, but was tied, so it put all its efforts into making a desperate move towards the Qinghua goal, surrounding it tightly. In this crowd, a ball came from the left, and Tang Wenwei headed it into the net. The score was 3-2, and the victory or defeat was determined. The performance of both sides was satisfactory and worth watching. The lineups are listed below:

Commercial News

Great Changes in the Gold Market Last Week 89

The result was a rebound of 8.2 taels

There were drastic fluctuations in the gold standard last week, with daily fluctuations ranging from five or six taels to over ten taels. People were unsettled, with varying demands and supplies. Initially, overseas silver markets continued to rise unabated, so the opening price for October fell to 690.5 taels, and a low price of 686.2 mace had already appeared. However, the local foreign exchange market was loose at first and then tight, soaring beyond 10 taels. Subsequently, prices rose and fell rapidly, fluctuating around 700 taels. Later, international silver markets and U.S. cotton, etc., generally declined, and the Shanghai market for British and American exchanges also appeared bullish. The market situation was strong, breaking through the 710 tael mark, and by Friday, it reached a high of 711.9 mace. Unexpectedly, local sentiment was panicked, affecting the market, breaking through the 700 tael mark. By the weekend, domestic and foreign exchange markets diverged, and the market softened, ultimately closing at 701.2 mace. Comparing this with the previous Saturday, there was a rebound of 8.2 mace, reversing a cumulative decline of over 50 taels over the past five weeks. The difference between the highest and lowest prices throughout the week was 25.7 taels, and the difference between the opening and closing prices was an increase of 10.07 taels. The spot market was active, and the Central Bank repeatedly absorbed gold, sometimes using U.S. dollars to offset it. The naked price initially increased by 11 taels and then decreased to a little over 9 taels. The amount of gold traded was approximately 24,000 taels. Guangbang Hengxing still held short positions, while the most prominent long positions were held by Yifeng Yong, Qian Changxiang, and Yuanxing Yong. As of yesterday, large bars of silver had already seen a rebound, and the gold market may be difficult to advance further. This state of inactivity was unprecedented. The total transaction volume for spot trading for the week was only 21,200 yuan. For futures, only the September contract was active, with more activity in the troop disbandment salt tax bonds. Other contracts were scarce, with daily transactions only around 1.5 to 1.6 million yuan, totaling 7,655,000 yuan. Although trading in the October contract had commenced, there were no transactions. Moreover, the environment was very dull before and after the month-end settlement. There were no new developments in diplomatic and domestic situations, and market sentiment became more cautious. Trading was scarce, and the supply and demand were balanced, causing prices to stagnate, which was rarely seen. Except for the consolidation 6 bonds, which had a difference of 2.5 yuan due to dividend exclusion, the remaining bonds fluctuated only around 6 to 7 jiao. As a result, compared to the previous week, there were mixed gains and losses. The consolidation 6 spot and the financial September contracts each fell by 7 to 8 jiao, while other futures contracts mostly gained around 3 to 4 jiao. Observing the bond market, the quiet environment and the brewing of various situations led to increasingly stagnant prices and increasingly scarce transactions. In the near future, if there are no new developments in the situation, it will be difficult to expect a turnaround in the market. Yarn and Cotton 93

General Sentiment is Bullish

The Yarn Market is Rising This Past Week

No Possibility of Genuine Demand Excitement

In the past week, the yarn market continued its upward trend. Due to the recovery of the European and American cotton industries, market prices rose, leading to positive sentiment. In addition, Rongxinghao bought in on dips, and the number of bales accumulated grew larger and larger. Bullish sentiment reached its peak, so there was a high point at the beginning of the week. Later, due to the decline of U.S. cotton, there were many rumors in Shanghai on the 3rd, and sentiment was volatile. General retail investors actively sold off, and the market showed slight weakness. On the weekend, U.S. cotton suddenly rebounded by dozens of pounds, and the bulls dragged in again. However, Changsha help settled 5,000 bales, all of which were absorbed by buyers. However, most people in the business community believe that domestic affairs are chaotic and genuine demand is sluggish, so they are consistently bearish and tend to go short. However, the overseas cotton market shows signs of recovery, and the domestic boycott movement is becoming more heated. Although there are unscrupulous merchants active, the patriotic sentiment in the interior is no less than in Shanghai. Therefore, local cotton yarn stocks are depleted, and inventories are very low. Yarn prices in Wuxi and Changzhou are better, so buyers have an even deeper concept of going long. The future situation is difficult to predict. Genuine demand among guest brokers is still quiet, and there is no excitement from any side, due to the continued difficulty in easing the economy. Statistics show that all brokers only bought 3,858 bales in the entire week, and the market was flat. The total transaction volume of the yarn standard for the week was 167,100 bales. The Vegetable Oil and Asphalt Market is Stable Due to Limited Inventory 98

Asphalt:　Each household has already started operating. It is assumed that there should be a batch of sales driven. However, the sluggish business of the paper candle industry is unexpected, causing the autumn sales that retailers were expecting to be less than half of what was expected. This is mainly because the commercial foundation of Shanghai has been greatly affected since the war. Such extravagant items are even more likely to be saved on. This is truly the autumn of "hundred industries withering". It is not just the candle industry. As for asphalt, although there is still some use in soap making, the peak season is in spring and summer. After autumn, orders have already decreased. After the Mid-Autumn Festival, it will be even less significant. Therefore, the candle sales route is entirely relied on in autumn and winter. Now that candle sales have declined, the market is of course depressed. However, stocks in various places are extremely low, so those with goods should not be anxious. Although sales are weak, sellers are still unwilling to lower prices. Moreover, the Hankou market is still strong. This is also due to the lack of goods, which keeps people from being fearful. It is heard that Chong Jing is still at 17.2 taels, Ping Jing at 16.8 qian, and Macheng also requires 17.2-3 taels. The stability of the situation can already be seen. Shanghai retailers have very little stock, so prices, although in line with Hankou, are said to be slightly negotiable.

The Tung Oil Trend is Stable 99

Tung oil has not been too sluggish due to foreign trade, so although there are occasionally weak trends, it quickly turns around. It can be seen that even if domestic sales are unreliable, foreign trade should continue uninterrupted. Recently, the market has softened slightly because foreign firms in Hankou are not handling many transactions. According to detailed letters from Hankou in recent days, each foreign firm is only handling dozens to at most 100 tons, with prices still at 18.6-7 qian by foreign standards. Although transactions are continuous, there are no large deals, so there is nothing special to report in the market. Domestic sales are preparing for the Mid-Autumn Festival, and those with inventory cannot avoid cautious inspections. The sales market seems quiet. Fortunately, prices have already fallen to the extreme, and there should be no further declines to expect. It is likely that there will be some activity after the holiday.

The Hardware and Tin Markets are Rising 100

Yesterday was Monday, and the hardware market had more retail sales than wholesale sales. The market situation seemed bustling on the surface, but large-scale transactions were still rare. Because there were no public telegrams from overseas, there were few changes in various markets. However, the tin market suddenly experienced a rapid rise yesterday. Prices for all goods rose by 2-3 taels. According to investigation, the reason for the rise was the increase reported in Singapore private telegrams. In addition, the London tin market is also advancing rapidly, so the Shanghai market followed suit.

New Galvanized Iron Sheet Coming Soon:　Regardless of whether it is No. 24 to No. 28, according to foreign firms, the new galvanized iron sheets are expected to arrive with over a thousand dan this Wednesday or Thursday, so there is no worry about a temporary shortage in the market. The current market price for No. 24 is 9.2 taels per dan, No. 26 is 10.095 taels, and No. 28 is 11.35 taels. It is said that only sporadic transactions have occurred in recent days.

The White Lead Market Has Passed Its Peak:　Since tea brokers stopped operating, the No. 2 white lead market has declined significantly. The No. 3 and 4 military factories have also not made any inquiries, so the market situation is very sluggish. No. 5 and 6 battery factories do a bit of business, which is enough to make do with the remaining situation. There has been no news about No. 7 and 8 for a long time. Although No. 9 and 10 have rebounded slightly, the amount is limited. The overall trend is that the situation is getting worse, and the decline in No. 2 is the most severe. It is currently estimated at 21.25 taels, which is a little over 1 tael less than before.
