Free Talk

Quotations from Ma Xiangbo, a 93-Year-Old Man

Political Parties Use People as Machines 102

— Jing Ji

On August 3rd, when Elder Xiangbo was seriously ill, I visited him. After pondering for a moment, he told me these words:

"Political parties and politicians, they exploit the people, believing that people are machines that can be driven. Therefore, they try every means to make themselves successful machine operators. Why do I advocate democracy? Because I know that everyone has a conscience. With a conscience, according to natural law, everyone can govern themselves. The people themselves are the masters."

Later, when Mr. Chen came to report on the Northeast issue, Elder Xiangbo gave another example to illustrate the difference between democracy and non-democracy, saying:

"I remember during the Franco-Prussian War, Prussian soldiers invaded French territory in large numbers, and all supplies were raised locally. The local people in France had to provide them. However, they all wrote an invoice at the current price, signed by the Prussian officer, and kept it. Later, when France paid reparations, it deducted these amounts and returned them to the people who suffered losses in the war zone. It seems that the people of that country value the spirit of democracy and put the people first. This has always been the case!"

"I also remember during the Taiping Rebellion, when the Red Turbans came to Shanghai, wealthy Shanghai families, such as the Yu family, were also forced to provide everything. However, afterward, the local officials instead accused them of communicating with the enemy, and as a result, they were all punished. Our country has never protected the people, always guarding against them. Even when the country is in danger and foreign enemies penetrate deep, it is the people who suffer. It seems that if we do not take the path of democracy, there is no fundamental way to save the country from disaster. Are the people of the whole country just going to sit back and watch our compatriots in the Northeast be oppressed?"

Thought Diary 103

— Jie Lu

丨A Few Lines for Self-Reflection丨

Since the establishment of the Republic of China, when memorial weeks are held in schools, institutions, and organizations, there must be a reading of the "Will" and "three minutes of silence". I think: We should certainly admire and remember Premier Sun Yat-sen’s revolutionary spirit. As the Grand Historian Sima Qian said, "High mountains are admired, and noble conduct is followed. Although we cannot reach them, our hearts aspire to them.” However, reading the will every day may be like a little monk chanting scriptures, with no heart. It really has no value! As for the three minutes of silence, perhaps there are some people who take advantage of this silence to silently think about how they missed hitting the white board yesterday, and the person to their left won a three-card-flush hand. How unlucky! Or, they might silently think: What should I buy to give to my lover when I take my salary home today? In these three minutes, if one had the ability to read minds, one could write a psychological novel of 100,000 words. Now I have a humble opinion that when holding memorial weeks, we can compile a few lines for self-reflection. Everyone can read them aloud once, with their eyes, mouths, and hearts engaged. Perhaps it will have some slight effect. In schools, self-reflection lines can be written on banners and hung in classrooms, like "school mottos," which will have an even better effect. Here are some self-reflection lines (with four examples to illustrate):

Have I forgotten the Japanese occupation of the three northeastern provinces?

Have I forgotten the January 28th Incident?

Have I forgotten the arduous resistance of the volunteers in the Northeast?

Have I ever bought enemy goods?

A Quick Sketch of the Racetrack 104

— Qian Taisheng

丨The Prosperous Gambling Den丨

On a certain day of a certain month, thanks to someone's kindness, I got a free ticket to the racetrack, and I had the honor of attending this grand event! It is something that must be recorded, but there's not much to record, so I'll just create a "quick sketch."

Stepping forward, the first thing I encountered was two or three doormen at the front gate. A tall-nosed man pointed with his finger and said, "Go through the side gate." Having never set foot in a racetrack before, I mistakenly walked through two or three iron gates. Along the road, all I saw were densely packed cars. Finally, after stumbling around, I entered the entrance. After walking in, I couldn't help but look back to see if this place was still a "forbidden zone!"

Entering the racetrack and climbing onto the stands, what a huge racetrack it was! Land is more precious than gold in Shanghai, yet they were able to carve out such an open space!

Wherever the signs for the twenty-some horses were displayed, large crowds of people were always gathered. There were gentlemen with protruding bellies, escorting their charming and graceful wives and mistresses. Whether they had blue eyes and tall noses, or flat noses and black hair, in short, they were all regular patrons of this place! At the places where "horse positions" were being bought, all I saw were red and green slips flipping in and out, and silver dollars clanging. Sudden wealth and sudden ruin were all determined by this one gamble!

The race started with twenty-five horses! Those riders in their colorful silk outfits all wanted to be the sole champion! Horses are just beasts, so how would they understand human tricks? They desperately unleashed their four hooves and galloped wildly through the flying dust. As they approached the finish line, two horses collided, and both riders and horses fell to the ground. The horses quickly righted themselves and stood up, but who paid attention to the people rolling on the ground?

Everyone's attention was focused on those fat necks, those protruding chests and bellies, and the binoculars hanging from them, watching to see if number thirty-six had won the race!

Oh, that big champagne, that small champagne, this eternally prosperous gambling den!

Popularization of Art 105

— Lu Kui

"Popularization of art" is something that everyone has been advocating recently. Indeed, art should be popularized, especially in modern China. The Chinese people of today need a kind of popular, noble, progressive, and mass-oriented art to transform their thinking. However, true mass art has not yet been produced. In this awkward transitional period, what should we use to bridge the gap? Some people advocate infusing new life into the old folk art shells or improving them ideologically to serve as nourishment for the people's spirit. The Tianyi Film Company's recently released "Variety Show Gathering" is a collection of songs, dramas, and variety acts that have been widely circulated among the people, as well as dances that have been introduced from the West. It presents them on the screen as a purely song and dance drama with sound. Besides the original and newly created material, many of the pieces use folk song scores with newly composed lyrics, such as the Taoist song "Fisherman and Woodcutter's Dialogue," the Northern Song "Autumn Chamber Complaint," the Suzhou ballad "Pitying Spring," as well as "Boatman's Song" and "Welcoming Spring Song." There is also a scene of "Su San Being Escorted," which is performed by twelve female stars using new-style song and dance methods to perform Peking opera, which is truly unique. I believe that the production of this film is a comprehensive compilation and organization of folk art. On the one hand, it provides entertainment for the masses, and on the other hand, it provides material for artists to explore. It does achieve some of the effects of "popularization of art" and is indeed a meaningful endeavor.

A Modern View of Buddhism 106

— Luan Zhen

丨The Bodhisattva is the Original Trendsetter丨

The word "modern" is the most fashionable term in this era. As long as something is related to the present, this word is used to describe it, and it can fully express everything, so no other adjectives are needed. Therefore, everything must be modern now, and if it is not modern, it is not enough to indicate that it is in line with the times.

However, this term is most often applied to women. They themselves strive to be modern, and people often mention modern women. Therefore, in this respect, a new origin has been discovered for the word "modern." If someone were to compile an encyclopedia, I think it would inevitably be included.

This is based on evidence from scriptures and has been verified. At the same time, this source comes from the consideration of those who specialize in studying the truth (?)—the so-called worshipers of Buddha and chanters of sutras. They say, "The Buddhist scriptures once recorded a fact: the Buddha sent the Venerable Ananda to beg for alms and preach the Dharma to save all living beings. He was entangled by demons, and the most dangerous time was when he was seduced by a woman named Matangi, almost causing him to break his vows, because she was a prostitute and the Venerable Ananda went to her as a customer." It is said that he went to save her, but without the Buddha's rescue, even the Venerable could not save himself. So, the "modern" of today comes from this, without a doubt, and the modern women of today are all demons!

"This great discovery should be known to modern men and women," the Bodhisattva would probably say.

Silver Threads (5) 107

— Jiang Hongjiao

(III)

The people of the whole town did not think she was a madwoman and distrust the stories she told, which were exaggerated ravings; because they had already seen the heroic and mighty photo of Regiment Commander Yuan in the newspapers, and had also read many records of the fierce fighting near this town.

The municipal committee summoned the local bullies, gentry, and other relatively wealthy residents and held several meetings, proposing to build a monument in the open space in front of the town's elementary school to commemorate the brave and resourceful Regiment Commander Yuan. This was because they had read a news item in the newspaper stating that this Yuan Renkai, the regiment commander, was from this town. Therefore, Zhu Bofang advocated engraving the four golden characters "Defending the Homeland" on the monument, and he would personally come to participate in the unveiling ceremony when the monument was completed. However, many people opposed the four characters he proposed, especially the older people, who said: The place of origin listed in the newspaper may not be accurate. News reporters often like to exaggerate, just like writing a novel. Because he had made contributions in this town, they said that he was a local. Where did we get a person named Yuan in this town? Therefore, "Defending the Homeland" should not be changed to "Defending the Nation."

At that time, there was an elementary school principal who was of the same faction as the municipal committee. He said: How could there be no one named Yuan living in the town? Isn't Yuan the Madwoman named Yuan? I believe the newspaper's report is correct. Their field reporters are the most accurate and quick in gathering news. How could they be wrong? We have such a hero in our town, and not to praise him would be too much of a loss of our own prestige.

"Haha! So, you also believe that Regiment Commander Yuan is Yuan the Madwoman's husband?" said the owner of a rice shop.

"Yuan the Madwoman is originally a native of this town, but she lived outside since she was a child, and then moved back to the town. Isn't this Regiment Commander Yuan also lived outside since he was a child?" The elementary school principal argued.

As a result of the discussion, it was certain that a monument had to be erected, costing approximately three thousand yuan to build. The large characters to be engraved were decided to be "Peace Throughout the Town," firstly to indicate that the merits were for the benefit of this town, secondly to commemorate that the monument was donated by this town, and thirdly that the town could secretly suppress evil and ward off demons. Finally, the chairman of the municipal committee added: "Everyone is here today. We can only treat the words of suppressing evil and warding off demons as private words."

"Don't pass it on to the government, otherwise, being refuted is secondary. Problems will also occur with my position as a member of the municipal committee. Everyone must help a lot!" After saying these words, the meeting was adjourned. Then, Zhu Bofang invited everyone to eat a bowl of noodles, and everyone was very happy, volunteering to donate money to each household, hoping to get as much as possible.

Scattered Notes on the Pillow 108

— Huo Xueming

I am a human, not a god, so I have desires, like all vertebrates. When I analyzed my true self on the pillow, I came to know myself.

I love spring flowers, I love fine wine, I love the stars of Shanghai, I love the charming smiles of summer nights. In the meantime, I also love reading the rhymes of poets, and like ordinary people, I love gold coins. And even more shocking to myself is that the articles I write have no other meaning than to deceive people.

Looking around at my friends, the honest souls they create in the deep of night with their pens have the same shape and color as mine in the mirror, and then I laugh.

I can no longer believe that there has ever been something in the world that is eternal and indestructible, because I am a human, not a god.

Lytton Arrives in Shanghai by Plane Yesterday, Wang and Song Represent the National Government to Offer Comfort 109

American and Italian Commissioners and Secretaries Arrive on the Same Flight

Left Shanghai This Morning to Return to Europe, Gu Weijun and Others Travel Together

Wang, Song, Luo, and Gu Held a Very Important Meeting Last Night

Lord Lytton, Chairman of the League of Nations Inquiry Commission, American Commissioner Major General McCoy and his wife, Italian Commissioner Count Magazari, along with Secretaries Aster, Coates, and Baird, accompanied by Zhang Xueliang's advisor, Donner, took off from Beiping at 10:15 yesterday morning on a Ford plane and arrived safely at Hongqiao Airport at 3:50 in the afternoon. The newly appointed Ambassador to France, Gu Weijun, Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie, Italian Ambassador Cianno, and others were all at the airport to welcome them. After disembarking, Lord Lytton was unwilling to express any opinions on the content of the report. However, it was learned from another source that the report had just been signed at 8:00 yesterday morning. Lord Lytton and others were then escorted by Mayor Wu and others to the Cathay Hotel. It was decided that they would travel to Europe this morning on the Italian postal ship "Gange."

The Situation Upon Arrival in Shanghai 110

Hongqiao Airport, which is usually desolate, became very lively yesterday due to the arrival of Lord Lytton and others, and security was also very tight. The head of the Shanghai office of the Chinese delegation to the League of Nations had previously notified the authorities of the Public Concession to jointly maintain order. Therefore, Indian police mounted patrols were stationed along Hongqiao Road, and Western and Chinese police were stationed at each intersection. The airport entrance was guarded by police from the Municipal Police Bureau, and sentries were distributed around the airport to strictly prohibit idlers from approaching. The welcoming party consisted of about 80 people, who arrived at the airport陆续 around 1:00 in the afternoon. The airport buildings were all destroyed during the Japanese invasion of Shanghai and have not yet been repaired, so the welcomers were all waiting on the grass. Around 2:00, Ambassador Gu and Mayor Wu also arrived by car and shook hands with the welcomers on the scene. After exchanging pleasantries with Gu and Wu, they walked and talked with Italian Ambassador Cianno. Newspaper reporters took pictures of them. At 3:45, a black dot appeared in the sky to the north of the airport. As it flew closer, the welcomers all craned their necks in anticipation. The huge Ford plane circled the airport twice and then landed safely at the south end of the field. The welcomers all gathered in front of the plane. Italian Commissioner Count Magazari was the first to disembark. Ambassador Gu, Mayor Wu, and Vice Minister Liu all shook hands with him to welcome him. Next were American Commissioner Major General McCoy and his wife, and British Commissioner Lord Lytton was the last to disembark. Lord Lytton wore a white canvas suit, held a cane, and looked radiant, but he was much thinner than when he arrived in Shanghai last time. Lord Lytton shook hands with Mayor Wu and others, his attitude was amiable, his smile was warm, and he repeatedly said that the trip was very pleasant. The reporters rushed to take pictures, and a film company was also on the scene to shoot a sound newsreel, asking Lord Lytton to give a speech. Lord Lytton laughed and said, "I have nothing to say." The Italian representative then continued, "Our words are finished." Everyone smiled brightly. After the photos were taken, they took cars to the Cathay Hotel.

Lytton's Silence 111

After Lord Lytton got off the plane, he shook hands with each of the welcomers and chatted with Gu Weijun, saying that he found the flight very pleasant, especially when he passed Mount Tai, the beautiful scenery caught his eye, like watching a famous painting, which was very fortunate. He then accepted the Fox Film Corporation's request to shoot a sound movie. At that time, the photographer asked Lee to give a simple speech about the investigation team. Lee replied that he had said everything he had to say about the investigation team and would never say another word in the future, and his attitude was unusually silent. Before leaving, Lee specifically returned to the plane, shook hands with the pilot, expressed his gratitude, and was very polite. After arriving at the Cathay Hotel, he did not meet with reporters from various newspapers and declined all social engagements. Therefore, the banquet that Mayor Wu had scheduled at his private residence last night was temporarily canceled.

Wang and Song's Visit 112

Wang Jingwei, a member of the Central Executive Committee, the newly appointed Ambassador to France, Gu Weijun, and Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie went to the Cathay Hotel at 5:20 in the afternoon to meet with Lord Lytton and left after talking for half an hour. Wang represented the government to offer comfort. Wang did not express anything about the content of the conversation. Acting President of the Executive Yuan Song Ziwen also visited Lord Lytton at 5:35 and left at 7:35. He also did not reveal a word about the content of the conversation. American Consul General Cunningham also visited American Commissioner Major General McCoy at 5:10 yesterday afternoon.

Visits to Wang by Various Important Figures 113

President of the Executive Yuan Wang Jingwei had already been discharged from the hospital and returned to his private residence the night before. Around 9:00 yesterday morning, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie and Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi visited him and then left. At 10:00, Acting President of the Executive Yuan Song Ziwen, accompanied by the Commander-in-Chief of the 19th Route Army Cai Tingkai, also visited Wang at his private residence. At 10:20, Wang, Song, and Cai took a car to Song's residence on Qiqi Road. Ambassador to France Gu Weijun visited Mayor Wu Tiecheng at Wanglu at 9:30 yesterday morning. At 10:50, he also rushed to Song's residence. They discussed matters until 11:50 before leaving together. According to Ambassador Gu, the matters discussed with the two presidents, Wang and Song, concerned the diplomatic policies and arrangements for receiving Lord Lytton and others. Later, Gu went to Li Boke's residence on Haige Road for a banquet hosted by Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie. Mayor Wu and four others were also in attendance. As for when President Wang will return to Nanjing, according to Wang himself, it will not be decided until the 6th.

Luo Wen'gan Arrives in Shanghai 114

Minister of Foreign Affairs Luo Wen'gan returned to Nanjing from Wuhan on the Xianghe Wheel yesterday afternoon. At 1:00 in the afternoon, he took a special train to Shanghai with Xu Mo, Political Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, Shen Jinding, Director of the Asian Department, and Ying Shangde, Chief of the General Affairs Department. He arrived at the North Station at 7:03 in the evening. Liu Chongjie, Permanent Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, and others went to welcome him. After getting off the train, Minister Luo went to visit Gu Weijun to discuss diplomatic issues. According to Luo, when Dr. Gu Weijun went south, he was in Wuhan and could not meet him, so he specially came to Shanghai to meet Gu and discuss everything. As for going to Wuhan to meet Chairman Jiang, it was also to discuss diplomatic countermeasures, and the content could not be disclosed.

Last Night's Meeting 115

Last night, various important figures agreed to gather at Song's residence on Qiqi Road to hold a final meeting on China's diplomatic policies in the League of Nations, so that a general conclusion could be reached. At 9:10 last night, Wang Jingwei first drove to Song's residence. At 9:40, Minister of Foreign Affairs Luo Wen'gan, accompanied by Vice Ministers Liu Chongjie and Xu Mo, and Gu Weijun, arrived in the same car. They immediately consulted with Song Ziwen on diplomatic countermeasures. Luo Wen'gan reported Chairman Jiang's opinions, and after careful discussion for an hour and a half, the final decision was made. Gu Weijun was to follow this final decision in Geneva to deal with everything at the League of Nations General Assembly.

Wang Jingwei's Statement 116

At 11:10 last night, Wang Jingwei told reporters from this newspaper when he left Song's residence: Tonight's (i.e., last night's) meeting here was to take advantage of Ambassador Gu Weijun's trip to Geneva to attend the League of Nations General Assembly to hold a final discussion on China's diplomatic policies in the League of Nations. A general conclusion has now been reached, and Ambassador Gu will handle League of Nations diplomacy based on these policies. The report of the investigation team emphasizes the upholding of justice, so it is beneficial to our side.

Signing of the Report 117

When a reporter from this newspaper met Gu Weijun last night, he said that the report of the investigation team was signed in Ping at 8:00 this morning (i.e., yesterday morning). The work of the investigation team has come to an end. Lord Lytton took a plane to Shanghai immediately after the signing ceremony. The report was sent to Geneva by the fastest route. When the reporter asked whether Lord Lytton brought it to Shanghai this time, he replied that he had not discussed this with Lytton.

Luo Wen'gan's Statement 118

Last night, a reporter from this newspaper met with Minister of Foreign Affairs Luo Wen'gan. He said that he did not meet with Lord Lytton because of the rush of time. Last night's meeting at Song's residence was entirely to discuss diplomatic issues, and there were concrete results. However, the matter was of great importance and could not be disclosed. He would wait until he had seen Ambassador Gu Weijun and Lord Lytton off from Shanghai tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning) before returning to Nanjing.

Scheduled to Leave Shanghai This Morning 119

Lord Lytton and his party have decided to leave Shanghai on the Italian postal ship "Gange," which is scheduled to set sail at 11:00 this morning, and travel to Geneva. Ambassador to France Gu Weijun will also travel on the same ship to take up his post. His wife, Ms. Huang Huilan, is still in Ping and is said to be traveling to France on the Italian ship "Conte Rosso," which will sail next month. Lytton and others are scheduled to board the ship on a ferry from the New Customs Wharf at 9:00 this morning. Various important figures, such as Wang Jingwei, Song Ziwen, Luo Wen'gan, Liu Chongjie, Xu Mo, and Wu Tiecheng, will all personally see them off. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce also notified all executive and supervisory committee members to gather at the New Customs Wharf before 8:30 this morning to see them off.

Commemorate the September 18th National Humiliation and Strive to Save the Country Through Aviation 120

The China Aviation Construction Association's Circular Telegram

The Standing Directors of the China Aviation Construction Association, Zhu Qinglan, Xiong Xiling, Yin Zhiling, and others, issued a circular telegram saying: To all newspapers, circles, organs, schools, and groups in the country, and to overseas Chinese compatriots, for your review. Since the Japanese bandits invaded and occupied the Northeast, and the Songhu War of Resistance, our national territory has been tainted. Although it is said that the Japanese pirates are rampant and disregard justice, the fact that our military preparations are lacking and our national defense is weak is the reason for inviting insult and disaster. During the Songhu Campaign, our 19th Route Army fought bravely and repeatedly defeated the fierce enemy. However, due to the lack of air defense, our soldiers lost the opportunity to annihilate the enemy. This is what Chief Weng, who defended Wusong, painfully said. It is a great sigh. Now, General Ma Zhanshan is fighting hard in Hailun and is also oppressed by enemy planes everywhere. He lacks the ability to resist, and his soldiers are scattered. Hearing this makes people feel grief and indignation. Comparing the two incidents, it is clear that without air force, there is no way to win, and without air force, defeat is inevitable. If we were to pass the ruins of Zhabei and Wusong, and try to imagine the ashes of the cities in the Northeast, could we not weep bitterly? Since the September 18th Incident, almost a year has passed. The lost territory has not been recovered, and the disaster has deepened. The bombing of Chaoyang has not stopped, and the number of enemy troops in Shanghai has increased again. The arrival of tyranny cannot be reversed. However, the way to save ourselves lies in human effort. Our association is making efforts to overcome the difficulties and strive to be effective. We believe that saving the country requires a strong national defense, and national defense requires a strong air force. The establishment of an air force depends on the joint efforts of our compatriots at home and abroad. Now, on this sorrowful anniversary of the September 18th Incident, there should be a thorough discussion of saving the country and building an air force. We offer four proposals, hoping that you will consider them. (1) Local daily newspapers, magazines, and other publications should focus on promoting aviation to save the country in their materials commemorating the September 18th National Humiliation. (2) All circles, organs, schools, and groups in the country, and overseas Chinese compatriots, should make speeches or performances on aviation to save the country the focus of their commemorative meetings for the September 18th National Humiliation. (3) All circles, organs, schools, and groups in the country, and overseas Chinese compatriots, should save the money spent on entertainment and banquets on September 18th in banks or money shops to be used for aviation construction funds. (4) All circles, organs, schools, and groups in the country, and overseas Chinese compatriots, should strive to build aviation on September 18th to strengthen national defense and relieve national distress. Alas, the national crisis has reached its extreme. The fate of survival hangs by a thread. We are all in the same boat. Can we not be terrified? Now, the people of the country also know how to save the country, and saving the country must involve aviation. The key is to put it into practice. Any of the above four points will be of great help. We hope that all patriotic compatriots will work together to achieve them. If you need to inquire about anything, please send a letter to the China Aviation Construction Association, Continental Shopping Center, Nanjing Road, Shanghai.

Temporary Martial Law in the City for the Communist International Youth Day Yesterday 121

Gatherings in West Shanghai and North Bund Were Dispersed

Only Reactionary Leaflets Were Seized, Evening Was Peaceful

Yesterday, "September 4th" was the Communist International Youth Day. The authorities of the Chinese Concession received advance notice that the Communists would hold a meeting at that time. In order to maintain local security, they temporarily declared martial law. Gatherings occurred in West Shanghai and North Bund, and were stopped. Many reactionary leaflets were seized in various places. The evening was peaceful. The details are as follows:

Temporary Martial Law (1) Chinese Concession: The Director of the Municipal Police Bureau, Wen Yingxing, received advance notice that reactionary elements would take the opportunity to riot on September 4th. In order to prevent this, he declared temporary martial law. All police officers of the police stations in South Shanghai, North Shanghai, West Shanghai, East Shanghai, and Pudong were armed and on duty. Double posts were set up on all major roads. Inspectors, detectives, female inspectors, and the police brigade were all on duty patrolling and inspecting pedestrians, especially in North Shanghai and West Shanghai, which were the strictest. The sentry patrol team of the Garrison Command also patrolled around the city. (2) French Concession: All Chinese and Western detectives in the police stations were ordered to be on duty. All iron gates on the border between the Chinese and French Concessions were kept open as usual to facilitate traffic, but armed detectives were stationed at the border crossings, and security was very tight. The iron gates would be temporarily closed if necessary, especially at the West Xinqiao and Xujiahui areas, which were the strictest. (3) Public Concession: All Chinese and Western detectives in the police stations were armed and on duty. The vehicle patrol team set out to patrol. Although yesterday was Sunday, all senior personnel were still on duty as usual, and security was tight, especially in East Shanghai, West Shanghai, and Nanjing Road, which were the strictest.

Dispersing Gatherings At 10:00 yesterday morning, in the jurisdiction of the Fourth District Police Station of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau in the West Shanghai and North Bund area, more than 100 people in the form of workers and students suddenly prepared to hold a meeting in an open space. The Tanziwan Police Station of the Fourth District Police Station had already deployed defenses and immediately dispatched armed police to disperse them. Therefore, the meeting did not take place, and only many reactionary leaflets such as "Letter to Workers on the September 4th International Youth Day" were seized.

Seizure of Leaflets After the temporary martial law was declared yesterday by the police stations in various districts of the Municipal Police Bureau, the police stations of the French Concession, and the police stations of the Public Concession, only red and green reactionary leaflets were seized in various places, such as "Letter to All Circles on the International Youth Day," "Workers' Booklets," "To Workers on Japanese Imperialism:::" and other small booklets. All have been filed for reference. The evening was peaceful.

Japanese Envoy Arrives in Shanghai 122

Still Emphasizing Restoring Amity, Coexistence, and Co-prosperity

The newly appointed Japanese Minister to China, Mr. Ariyoshi Akira, and his wife arrived in Shanghai yesterday at 3 PM aboard the Nagasaki Maru. The Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Yano, Japanese Consul-General Murai, Japanese legation secretary Ariyoshi, Military Attaché Iwamatsu, Vice-Consul Shirai, and many representatives of the Japanese community gathered at the Waibaidu Bridge Wharf to welcome them. The Japanese military and administrative authorities also dispatched several gendarmes and naval landing forces to be stationed inside and outside the wharf for security. The Shanghai Municipal Police also sent Western and Japanese police to maintain order. After disembarking, Minister Ariyoshi immediately proceeded by car to the official residence on Avenue Pichon. The date for his presentation of credentials in Beijing has not yet been decided.

Issuing a Statement Whenever new Japanese envoys arrive in Shanghai, they always express the idea of Sino-Japanese amity, coexistence, and co-prosperity. Upon his arrival in Shanghai yesterday, Minister Ariyoshi reiterated, "I am determined to transform the current difficult relationship between China and Japan into a restoration of the former state of amity and to establish a foundation for the two countries' coexistence and co-prosperity." However, the method for achieving this hope was not explained by Minister Ariyoshi, as he was in transit yesterday. When inquiring among the general Japanese community, it was said that the so-called restoration of amity excludes Manchuria and Mongolia, and the idea of direct negotiations is even more虚無漂渺 [empty and vague]. Minister Ariyoshi's statement issued yesterday is as follows: "Although I have been appointed as the Minister to China during this difficult period in our two countries' relations, I deeply feel the weight of responsibility. I am now determined to transform this difficult relationship into a restoration of the former state of amity and to establish an Oriental peace based on the keynote of coexistence and co-prosperity between the two countries. I will exert all my efforts to achieve this. I believe that friendly relations between the two countries can only be realized through mutual and full understanding of each other's positions and through both parties working together to adequately meet each other's national needs. Fortunately, I have served in China for many years, and I was able to fulfill my duties and avoid overstepping boundaries on many problems I encountered, based on the aforementioned principles and with the assistance of various sectors of Chinese society. I still take great comfort in this matter. I aspire to base my handling of various issues between the two countries on my past understanding of the Chinese situation, as well as my understanding of the positions of both countries gained from fair observation during my overseas postings. I hope that gentlemen from all sectors of Chinese society, as well as people from all walks of life, will sympathize with my intentions and provide full assistance. This is what I earnestly hope for," etc.

Japanese Envoy Ariyoshi Akira and his wife Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Ariyoshi's Brief Biography Ariyoshi Akira graduated from Tokyo Higher Commercial School in 1898, obtained consular qualifications, and came to China in the same year, serving as a probationary consul in Hankou. He was later transferred to Chemulpo, Korea, as a probationary consul. In 1901, he was transferred to the London Consulate. In 1904, he was transferred to Busan, Korea, as a full consul. In 1908, he was promoted to Second Secretary of the Japanese Embassy in Paris. In 1909, he served as Consul-General in Shanghai. In 1926, he was promoted to Ambassador to Brazil. He returned to Japan in 1930. In August of this year, he succeeded Shigemitsu Mamoru as the Minister to China.

Japanese Naval Commander Sakonji Expected to Arrive in Shanghai Today 123

Five Japanese Warships Currently in the Huangpu River

The commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, Sakonji, is expected to arrive today from Hankou aboard the flagship Izumo. Of the warships belonging to the First Expeditionary Unit of the Yangtze River, only the flagship Ataka remains docked in Shanghai, along with the cruisers Tenryū and gunboat Toba, which arrived last Friday from Hankou and Jiujiang. The three destroyers of the 24th Division, namely, the Yanagi, Momo, and Tsuta, sailed out of Shanghai yesterday afternoon. Therefore, there are only four vessels in the Huangpu River, including the light cruiser Tokiwa, which is scheduled to return to Japan on the 7th. The rumor that nineteen Japanese warships have been concentrated in the Huangpu River, including a torpedo boat of the 15th Division, is purely unfounded and not to be believed.

Wen Yingshing's Resignation Approved, Mun Hung-en Appointed to Succeed Him by the Municipal Government 124

Sworn into Office This Morning

Police Commissioner Wen Yingshing, due to the embezzlement by Han Jin, the secretary of the bureau, and Chang Shao-yi, the head of the remittance section, submitted a sincere resignation to Mayor Wu, taking responsibility for the matter, which has been approved. Mayor Wu has appointed Mun Hung-en to succeed him, and the appointment was issued last night, while also submitting a request to the National Government for formal appointment. The new Police Commissioner Mun is scheduled to be sworn into office at the Municipal Police Bureau this morning. Mun, styled Duiting, is from Wenchang County, Guangdong Province, and is 40 years old. He graduated from the Yunnan Military Academy. He initially served as a staff officer in the General Headquarters of the Guangdong Bandit Suppression Army. During Chen Jiongming's rebellion, Mayor Wu served as the commander-in-chief of the Bandit Suppression Army and led troops to suppress the rebels under the command of General Sun Yat-sen. Mun served as a staff officer and recovered Bao'an. He was then transferred to serve as the second commander of the First Route Army. In the eleventh year of the Republic [1922], he aided Fujian.

Newly Appointed Police Commissioner Mun Hung-en

Photo by the New Sound Photography Studio

He recovered Fuzhou and served as a lieutenant colonel, battalion adjutant, and battalion commander in the Bandit Suppression Army in Ren Dong Road. In the thirteenth year of the Republic [1924], he served as a battalion commander in the Guangdong Provincial Guard Army. He returned east to suppress the Yang Liu Rebellion and was promoted to regimental commander, and then to commander of the 17th Division of the National Revolutionary Army. During the Northern Expedition, he followed Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek and recovered Nanchang, and was promoted to major general and regimental commander. In the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], he recovered Nanjing, and was promoted to commander of the 7th Division for his meritorious service. After the Northern Army was defeated, Mun led his entire division in pursuit, fighting battles across Jiangsu, Anhui, Shandong, and Hebei, reaching as far as Machang, Tianjin, with victories everywhere. He is known for his calm, resolute character and strategic thinking, and for his diligence in handling affairs. He has been with Mayor Wu for the longest time, and Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek also highly values him. He was ordered by the National Government to go to Europe for observation, interning with various French military units. Last year, he returned to China and served as a military advisor in the Military Advisory Council and as a research committee member at the Army Infantry School.

Commander Cheng Changkui of the Northeast Cavalry First Detachment sent representatives to Shanghai a month ago to receive a large batch of clothing and other items from the Northeast Volunteer Army Rear Area Support Association. Provisional Meeting of Shareholders in the Commercial Press 129

Provisional Resolution to Reduce Capital and Amend Articles of Association

The Commercial Press held a provisional meeting of shareholders yesterday at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's meeting hall on North Henan Road. A total of 1,113 shareholders, including representatives, attended, holding 32,307 shares and 28,760 voting rights. The meeting began at 3:30 PM, with Mr. Zhang Jusheng presiding. The special agenda was to discuss the reduction of capital and the amendment of the articles of association. After a lengthy discussion by the shareholders, it was resolved that after offsetting the company's losses, there was a net loss of over 2.124 million yuan. The capital of 5 million yuan was reduced to 3 million yuan, leaving a remaining loss of over 124,000 yuan. If there is a surplus in the 21st year of the Republic [1932], it should be used to offset the losses first. In addition, the various articles of the company's articles of association were also voted on separately and passed. The chairman stated that the number of shareholders attending the meeting today did not exceed half, and according to the law, the resolution to reduce capital and amend the articles of association passed today should be treated as a provisional resolution, and a second provisional meeting of shareholders should be convened on a scheduled date for a vote. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Feng Bingnan Resigns as Director of the Municipal Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall 131

Feng Bingnan's Three Letters of Resignation to Jiao Yitang Expressing His Firm Resolve to Resign as Director of the Municipal Traditional Chinese Medicine Hall, Recorded as Follows: (1) "To Mr. Yitang, I was negligent in entertaining you when you honored me with your visit the other day. I deeply apologize. When Mr. Zhao arrived here last night, he recounted your intentions in detail, which filled me with inexplicable gratitude and fear. The reason why I have hesitated to accept the position of director of the branch hall of the National Medical Institute is that I am burdened with mundane affairs and have no time to spare. In addition, my health is naturally weak, and even a slight exertion causes me to suffer from insomnia. I have been deeply concerned about the difficulties of the times for years, and I only blame myself for my inadequacy. Moreover, I always take responsibility for everything I do and dare not be perfunctory, which is why I am not liked by others and suffer even more myself. Therefore, I want to gradually withdraw from worldly affairs and care for my mother to the end of her days. I am not using this as a means to make myself seem noble. If, as you say, I can hire someone to take my place, then it would be a mere formality, and I would feel uneasy in my heart. Moreover, if I hire someone to represent me, I would still be legally responsible, so what would be the point? I believe that organizing traditional Chinese medicine is of great importance to our country's cultural undertakings and social well-being. At the beginning, it is necessary to select someone with both virtue and reputation and enthusiasm to promote public opinion and achieve twice the result with half the effort. I am not capable and am busy all day long, so how can I bear this responsibility? I have declined repeatedly because I know myself very well, and I have no choice. I am honored to be known and dare not not express myself fully. Please do not publish this to avoid revealing any trace. I hope that you will cherish yourself. Respectfully, Feng Bingnan, August 29th night." (2) "To Mr. Yitang, I was deeply touched by Mr. Hu Jurand's visit yesterday, conveying your kind intentions. However, my inability to assume the position of director of the branch hall is not out of modesty. I am caught up in mundane affairs and have no time to spare. I am already struggling to cope with my personal business affairs. If I were to take on this position as well, I would not have the energy. If it were merely a formality, I would not be able to live up to your expectations, nor would I be able to live up to the expectations of the medical community, nor would I be able to find peace of mind. After much hesitation, I dare not accept this commission. The importance of this position and the relationship between this matter and the country's culture and social welfare have been fully stated in my previous letter. I admire the perseverance of your leadership, and if I do not hold the position but assist from the side as a member of society, there is no problem. However, if I am given the position of director, I will not accept it under any circumstances. In addition to entrusting Mr. Hu to convey my humble thoughts, I dare to repeat my foolishness out of respect for your understanding. I return the appointment and hope that you will understand. Respectfully, Bingnan, August 31st. Attached is the returned appointment." (3) "To Mr. Yitang, I have missed your teachings for several days. I recently saw a newspaper report about the Shanghai National Medical Institute branch hall, which mentioned that I have been appointed as the director of the main hall. I have repeatedly declined this matter in person and asked that it not be published. I have also entrusted Mr. Hu Jurand and my secretary Mr. Zhao Yongbai to convey everything on my behalf and have sent two letters to you at the end of last month, detailing why I was unable to accept the appointment. However, my request has not been heeded, and it has still been published, which fills me with great fear. In addition to sending separate letters to various newspapers to clarify, I still hope that you will withdraw your order and appoint another capable person. Respectfully, Feng Bingnan, September 4th."

American Chamber of Commerce Opposes International Telegraph Rate Increase 133

Former Director of the International Telecommunications Bureau, Mr. Lu Guixiang, Expresses His Opinion

Hua Dong News Agency reports that the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai has expressed its opposition to the proposal to increase international telegraph rates between Shanghai and various countries, which will be discussed at the International Telegraph and Wireless Radio Conference in Madrid, Spain, on the 10th of this month. Their reasons are roughly divided into three points: (1) The world economy is in a state of recession, and cannot afford to bear the expense of increased telegraph rates. (2) International telegrams between Shanghai and various countries are already more expensive than those between Europe and America, while the volume of business between Europe and America is better than that between Shanghai and various countries. (3) Due to the depreciation of the Chinese currency, the exchange losses on telegraph fees here are very large, making it difficult to pay increased fees. A reporter from Hua Dong News Agency specifically visited Mr. Lu Guixiang, the former director of the International Telecommunications Bureau, to inquire about his opinion, and he said the following: "The International Telecommunications Conference to be held in Madrid in September of this year is to discuss the merger of the telegraph and radio conventions, as well as the revision of the attached operating rules. The issue of increasing international telegraph rates is not within the scope of the conference's discussion. The claim that the conference will propose increasing telegraph rates between Shanghai and various countries is unfounded. However, at this conference, many participating countries have proposed fundamental revisions to the original international code telegram system, which may affect the price issue. International code telegrams have always been divided into two types, A and B. Type A is limited to ten letters, with three vowels in the middle to facilitate pronunciation. The fee is charged at the full price of a plain language word. Type B is limited to five letters, and the fee is charged at three-quarters of the full price of a plain language word in the European region, and two-thirds in non-European regions. Telegraph authorities and companies in various countries find it difficult to calculate the number of words and charge fees when code words are divided into two types. Moreover, ten letters connected to each other in Type A code words have no meaning and no melody, making them prone to errors. The correction procedures take more time. Countries such as Greece, the Netherlands, and Hungary have similar proposals, advocating that all should be limited to five letters. The Ministry of Transportation of our country also has this proposal, advocating that there should be only one type of code word, with each word consisting of five letters, with at least one vowel. The fee collection method, regardless of whether it is in the European or non-European region, is uniformly charged at three-quarters of the full price of plain language. If this method is adopted, then international code telegrams in non-European regions will increase the fee by one-eighth compared to the old Type B method. This may be the crux of the opposition of the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai. However, in my opinion, the silver fees collected for code telegrams are actually very cheap compared to plain language telegrams. Although plain language is limited to a maximum of fifteen letters, in reality, few words in various languages are composed of fifteen letters. For example, the long sentence 'It is reported that a proposal for the increasing cable and radil chargesto and from Shanghai will be up for Consideralion at the conference of internatioaltelgrnph union which opens at MADRID ONseptember tenth,' contains thirty-seven plain language words and a total of one hundred and eighty letters, averaging less than five letters per word. If the short intervals in the telegram are deleted without hindering the clarity of the text, the average is always about seven and a half letters. Code words with five letters can possibly express the effect of two plain language words. Therefore, calculated by letters, code words should be one-third cheaper than plain language. Calculated by effect, even if code words are charged twice as much, it would be fine. This time, our country proposes that one code word should be calculated at three-quarters of the full price of plain language, only unifying the fees for non-European and European regions, and there is still no intention to increase the telegram fee. Whether it can pass depends on the opinions of the participating countries, and our country can only obey the majority. As for the American Chamber of Commerce's claim that the international telegraph business between Shanghai and various countries is not as good as that between Europe and America, if it refers to the sending and receiving via submarine cables, then I do not know. If it refers to the international radio station's wireless radio business, then I dare not agree. Checking between Shanghai and San Francisco and between Shanghai and Berlin/Paris, each telegram only takes eight minutes, and at the latest no more than fifteen minutes. During last year's League of Nations General Assembly in Geneva, the wireless radio telegram between Shanghai and Geneva also only took ten minutes. Such business is not much less even compared to Europe and America. As for the global recession and the loss of payment in Chinese currency, these are universal situations and cannot be regarded as reasons. The global recession affects the finances of various countries and various telegraph companies, and China's influence by the preciousness of gold and the cheapness of silver is well known to everyone. Taking the international radio station as an example, the cost of the equipment and materials used are all in gold, and the expenditure in national currency has almost doubled in recent years. How can one only blame the loss of international telegraph fees due to the conversion into national currency?"

Organizing a Committee to Handle the Matter

Since the government promulgated the amnesty ordinance, the Shanghai Local Court and the Special District Court have both complied and handled it one after another, reducing or exempting crimes according to the severity of the crime and the sentence, which is currently in progress. This righteous act of the association not only gives the prisoners a new path to self-renewal, but also benefits social order. The native place associations in this city are numerous, and after the association's advocacy, there will surely be those who follow suit, which is a good news in the sound of the amnesty.

Local News Two

Verdict of the Second Special Court on the Yun Case 135

Yun Huifang, a patriotic person, because Maochang Cotton Fabric Shop, opened by Ningbo native Shen Maochun at 347 Min'guo Road in the French Concession, was privately selling enemy goods and secretly selling them, hindering patriotic unity. After warnings by letter proved ineffective, on the 5th of last month at 9:00 PM, he carried a hand grenade to the shop and threw it as a warning, destroying the glass floor. At that time, Yun fled into the Chinese territory and was intercepted by a patrol officer and taken to the bureau. Subsequently, the political department of the French Concession police sent detectives to the Public Security Bureau to bring Yun back to the police station for investigation and escort him to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. After Judge Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Court held a trial, with the defendant represented by a lawyer, a verdict was reached. Yun Huifang was sentenced to two months of imprisonment with a two-year reprieve. These details have been published in various newspapers. However, Yun is also related to a bombing case at a certain coal shop on Xinza Road in the Public Concession. The Public Concession police have brought him to the First Special District Court for questioning. Because legal points of contention have not been resolved, the formal trial has not yet begun. The full text of the Second Special Court's verdict is recorded below for the perusal of interested parties.

Criminal Verdict of the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Local Court, No. 264, 21st Year Xie Di Zi, verdict against the defendant Yun Huifang, male, 16 years old, native of Changzhou, occupation typesetter at a printing bureau, residing at 207 Mei'an Lane, Park Road, retained defense lawyers Zhao Chen, Shen Junru, and Liu Hongxun. The above-listed defendant was prosecuted by the police department for offenses such as obstruction of freedom and damage. The court's trial verdict is as follows: (Main Text) Yun Huifang is sentenced to two months of imprisonment with a two-year reprieve for the crime of threatening others with harm to life and property, causing a danger to safety. A package of hand grenade fragments is confiscated. (Facts) Yun Huifang learned that Maochang Foreign Goods Shop at 347 Min'guo Road was selling Japanese goods. On August 5th of this year, at approximately 9:00 PM, seeing that there was no one in the shop, he threw a hand grenade into it as a warning. Unexpectedly, the hand grenade exploded immediately, causing damage to the glass floor and other items. Yun Huifang fled not far before being apprehended by Chinese patrol officers and taken to the bureau. Subsequently, he was taken back by the French Concession police for investigation, along with the hand grenade fragments, and prosecuted in court under Articles 158, 161, and 382 of the Criminal Code. (Reasons) In this case, the defendant Yun Huifang has confessed to throwing a hand grenade at Maochang Foreign Goods Shop, and he was apprehended on the spot by Chinese police. The facts are extremely clear. However, according to the defendant's testimony, throwing the hand grenade was only a warning not to sell Japanese goods, and there was no intention to harm anyone. Because there were many people during the day, he was afraid of hurting someone, so he threw the grenade at night when the shop employees were outside enjoying the cool air. Upon investigation, the defendant threw the grenade at Maochang Foreign Goods Shop with the intention of intimidating the shop owner. The resulting harm was only to the safety of the shop. This does not fall under the circumstances stipulated in Article 158 of the Criminal Code. The defendant should be found guilty of violating Article 319 of the same law. As for being involved in the "Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group," according to the defendant's testimony, the "Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group" only consisted of himself and a Mr. Cai. There was no so-called organization, nor any articles of association. He himself created the name, and the purpose was only to warn treacherous merchants. Since the defendant claims that the so-called "Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group" only had two members, it is difficult to consider it an association with the purpose of committing crimes. He cannot be convicted under Article 161 of the Criminal Code. There is no doubt about this. Regarding the damage portion, Shen Maochun of Maochang Foreign Goods Shop reported it to the police department in writing, specifying that five pieces of glass and one strip of flooring were damaged. This should be considered a legitimate accusation and accepted. However, the damage to the glass floor was the result of committing another crime. According to Article 74 of the Criminal Code, compared to Article 382 of the same law, the heavier penalty under Article 319 should be applied. The defendant Yun Huifang was born on the 16th day of the 11th month of the lunar calendar in the sixth year of the Republic. Counting to August of this year, he has not yet reached the age of sixteen. The original sentence should be reduced by one-half. Furthermore, the defendant's criminal act was motivated by righteous indignation and is excusable. The original sentence should be further reduced by one-half. Moreover, the defendant has not been sentenced to detention or a more severe punishment. This meets the conditions for a reprieve. A reprieve should be granted. The seized hand grenade fragments are contraband and should be confiscated. Based on Articles 319, 74, 30 paragraph 2, 77, 87 paragraph 1, 90 paragraph 1, and 60 paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code, and Articles 315 and 320 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the verdict is as stated in the main text. Prosecutor Wu Xiaoke attended the court to perform his duties. If dissatisfied with the verdict, an appeal may be filed with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court within ten days from the day following the delivery of the verdict. August 11th, 21st Year of the Republic of China, Judge Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Court (seal).

Three Workers Tragically Die While Repairing the Seawall 136

Japanese Shell Buried in Soil

Detonates Upon Contact, Flesh and Blood Fly

Many sections of the seawall around the Shizilin Fort in Wusong were damaged by Japanese artillery fire. With the autumn tide approaching, the situation is precarious. Wan Kaijia, director of the Baoshan Seawall Works, has been hiring workers to rush repairs in recent days. Yesterday morning, around 11:30 AM, three laborers, Bian Guifang, Jiang Wanyu, and Zhou Zhiming, were working on the seawall at the northern end of Shizilin, using rakes to dig up soil. Unbeknownst to them, an unexploded Japanese shell was buried in the soil. They did not notice it during their work. Upon contact, it immediately exploded. The three workers were torn apart, and all died instantly. After the incident, it was immediately reported to the Baoshan County government. County Magistrate Sun dispatched investigation officer He Cheng to the scene. It was determined that the deceased, Bian Guifang, Jiang Wanyu, and Zhou Zhiming, all had ruptured abdomens and flowing intestines, and their limbs were incomplete. The scene was ghastly. It was confirmed that they had been killed by the explosion. The foreman was ordered to collect the bodies.

Water Boiler Explosion at Mei Xin Dye Factory Injures People 137

Three Dye Workers Scalded by Boiling Water

Two Sections of Chimney Soar into the Sky

Nearby Electric Lights Extinguished

Mei Xin Silk Fabric and Electric Dye Factory, located at 64 Guling Road, has been in operation for three years. It was founded by Dai Jinyu, a native of Shaoxing, and the business is doing well. Yesterday evening, around 9:50 PM, the dye factory workers were still working late because of a large backlog of goods. Unexpectedly, the water boiler in the rear building, due to excessive heat, had a pressure relief pipe malfunction, causing it to explode suddenly with a sound like a cannon. Neighbors were awakened from their dreams. Boiling water from the boiler splashed everywhere like waves, causing severe burns to dye workers Yu Jinfang, Zhou Jinshui, and Wang Arong, who were nearby. They immediately fainted and fell to the ground. At the same time, two sections of the iron chimney on the roof of the furnace room were blown into the sky. One section landed on the roof of house number 109 in Dehua Lane behind the factory, collapsing one stove awning. Another section flew towards Park Road, severing electric wires at the intersection of Park Road and Guling Road. It then fell on the roof of Jusheng Rice Shop at 678 Park Road, piercing the roof. As a result, the electric lights along the road in various lanes were completely extinguished. Hua Pu, officer number 3914, on guard duty at the scene, immediately blocked traffic to prevent electrocution. He reported to the police station, which dispatched officers to investigate and provide assistance. The electric company was notified to send technicians to repair the damage as quickly as possible. The electricity was restored that evening. The three dye workers who were scalded by boiling water were transported by Hua Pu's car to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, their injuries are critical, and their lives may be in danger.

Fire Aboard the Xinning Shao Steamer in the Cargo Hold Extinguished 138

Passengers Were Startled, but Fortunately All Are Safe

Streetcar and Ambulance Collide, Injuring People

The Xinning Shao steamer of the Ningshao Steamship Company, which travels between Shanghai and Ningbo, encountered a fire in the cargo hold on its return trip from Ningbo. Fortunately, the fire was discovered not far from Shanghai. The crew responded effectively, preventing the fire from spreading. Although the cargo suffered losses and the passengers were startled, it was a stroke of good fortune amidst misfortune. However, as a result of this incident, a collision between an ambulance and a streetcar caused a disaster in which many firefighters were injured. The details are described below.

Fire Breaks Out in the After Hold: The Xinning Shao steamer departed from Ningbo for Shanghai on the afternoon of the 3rd, carrying a shipment of cotton, which was divided into the middle and after holds. The hold was normal when the ship left Ningbo. Around 2:00 AM that night, smoke suddenly appeared in the cargo in the after hold. The crew discovered the smoke and reported it to the captain, first mate, and second mate. Under the captain's orders, the hatch was quickly sealed, and the after hold was isolated from the middle hold to prevent the fire from spreading. The fire extinguishers on board were used to pump extinguishing agents into the hold, and the ship sped towards the port. The first mate sent a telegram requesting assistance.

Ship Arrives in Shanghai: The Wusong Radio Station received the telegram about the ship's fire and forwarded it to the company. The company reported to the customs and notified the Nanshi Fire Brigade to have fire trucks waiting at the Ningshao Wharf for the ship's arrival. However, after the hold was sealed and extinguishing agents were injected, the fire gradually died down. The ship entered Wusong at 6:40 AM, and when it arrived at the wharf at 8:00 AM, the hold was no longer smoking. After the ship docked, the passengers disembarked first, and then the hatch was opened to spray water.

Minimal Cargo Damage: When the hatch was opened, the hot, humid air inside rushed out. Four firefighters on board were suffocated and collapsed on the ship. They were rescued and brought ashore by fellow firefighters. The Public Concession was telegraphed to send ambulances to transport the injured. The fire trucks then sprayed water into the after hold. The fire was extinguished quickly. Upon inspection, only two bales of cotton were burned, causing minimal damage. The other goods, which were not burned, suffered significant water damage and are currently being unloaded and inspected.

Car Collision Causes Accident: An ambulance, numbers 2 and 3, from the Public Concession was heading to Nanshi when it approached the Grand Clock Tower in the French Concession. There, it encountered streetcar number 10, which was speeding west from the Bund. The ambulance was traveling south to north. The two vehicles approached each other, and both attempted to yield. However, while the drivers were hesitating to move forward or backward, the ambulance had already entered the streetcar tracks and was violently struck in the side. The ambulance body was immediately damaged, and all the glass was destroyed. The driver of the ambulance, Wang Wenyu, and firefighter personnel, including a Mr. Ying and a Mr. Zhang, were injured in the head. Two other people, a Mr. Zhang and a Mr. Liu, were injured in their hands. One passenger in the streetcar was injured in the face. The Red Cross arrived, and the injured were transported to the hospital. The damaged vehicles were towed away.

Implementing Agencies Changed to Offices Attached to Consulates

Consular certification of cargo manifests was implemented on the first of this month. The original plan was for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send personnel to various treaty ports in foreign countries to handle the matter. Yesterday, the Central News Agency quoted Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Liu Chongjie as saying that due to financial constraints at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the implementation would be handled by offices attached to Chinese consulates in various countries. Special personnel would no longer be dispatched separately.

Islamic Organizations Commemorate Ma Fuxiang 140

The various mosques in Shanghai previously held scripture readings and prayers for Ma Fuxiang on the 26th of this month. Yesterday (September 4th), they held a memorial meeting at the Islamic Association. The Chinese Islamic Association, the Shanghai Qingzhen Board of Directors, the Qingzhen West Mosque, South Mosque, and North Mosque within Shanghai city, the Qingzhen Foreign Mosque outside the city, and various Qingzhen mosques, as well as the Shanghai Islamic Classics Institute, Shanghai Dunhua Elementary School, Islamic Orphanage, and Muslim community members all attended the memorial service at the association. The meeting began at 10:00 AM, and the rituals were performed. Mr. Ha Shaofu was elected as chairman, and he reported on the purpose of the meeting and the achievements of Mr. Ma, followed by Elder Ha Decheng reading an elegy (in Arabic). Sugar Industry Association Again Writes to Customs Superintendent Regarding Unfair Public Auction, Requesting Justice 145

The Shanghai Sugar Industry Association, based on a letter from its member Guangyuan, states that George, the Customs Commissioner of the General Affairs Department of the Jianghai Customs, engaged in questionable practices during the public auction of confiscated white sugar. It details the irregularities and again requests the Customs Superintendent to uphold justice and provide a fair resolution. The original letter is transcribed below:

"Having received your letter of the 13th of this month, regarding the requested thorough investigation of the public auction of confiscated white sugar, the Customs Commissioner replied that the Yuanji firm's bid was altered before it was opened and that the auction was not conducted publicly. He claims that the opening and decision were handled by the Customs Commissioner of the General Affairs Department, who considers Guangyuan firm to be unfamiliar with customs regulations and therefore should not rashly accuse them of shady dealings. He requests that you express your apology to the Customs, and until this is done, all matters related to your firm's dealings with the Customs will be ignored. We were asked to investigate and report back.

Having informed Guangyuan of this, we received a reply stating that the Customs Commissioner admits that the auction of the confiscated sugar was not public and that the bid was indeed altered. However, he defends the lack of public opening by claiming it is the usual practice of the Jianghai Customs. We question whether there is any explicit provision in the customs regulations for this. Even if such a regulation exists, it is questionable whether it aligns with the spirit of a public auction. Furthermore, regarding the alteration of the bid before it was opened, we request that sufficient evidence be provided. If this were true, then all bids submitted to the Customs could be altered before being opened, which is unreasonable.

There are two points that raise doubts about whether the bid was altered before it was opened: (1) Yuanji's original bid was four taels and four mace, but suddenly became five taels and one mace; (2) The price of five taels and one mace was precisely three fen higher than our bid. Considering this, we must request that your association continue to petition the Customs Superintendent to review and avoid being deceived by clever disguises.

Furthermore, in our letter of the 4th of this month, we requested that the Customs Superintendent conduct a thorough investigation. We were not concerned about our losing the bid, but we feared that if the Customs' public auction of confiscated goods lacked fairness and protection, it would deter legitimate bidders and allow cunning individuals to take advantage, ultimately resulting in a loss of national revenue. Therefore, our request for rectification is in the public interest, not for personal gain. However, the Customs Commissioner demands that we apologize and threatens to ignore all our future dealings with the Customs. This abuse of power is evident, and we request that your association again petition the Customs Superintendent to uphold justice."

Based on the above, the association believes that the original intention of the investigation is to prioritize the national treasury, not to recover a lost bid, and that the alteration of the bid raises concerns. Conducting an auction without public opening is not conducive to preventing corruption. Therefore, we again request that you, the Superintendent, provide a fair resolution. We also hope that you will appropriately correct the Customs Commissioner's abuse of power to uphold justice and benefit the national treasury. We earnestly hope for this outcome.

Shen Xin Textile Factory Worker with Amputated Arm Awarded 1,000 Yuan in Compensation by Special Court 148

Application of Article 45 of the Factory Law

Wu Genyun, a mechanic in the weaving room of Shen Xin No. 6 Cotton Mill in Yangshupu, had his right arm severed by a machine belt during work. Although the wound healed, the arm could not be reattached, resulting in permanent disability. Wu argued that his injury was solely due to the prolonged use and failure to replace the machine belt, and that the factory was undeniably responsible. He hired lawyers Yang Linzhi and Ye Shaoying to file a lawsuit against the factory, seeking 3,000 yuan in compensation and 1,900 yuan in disability benefits under the government-promulgated Factory Law. After several court hearings in the First Special District Court, the court concluded that Article 45, Paragraph 1, Section 2 of the Factory Law was applicable and ordered the defendant to pay the plaintiff 1,000 yuan in benefits as compensation. The claim for compensation for losses was rejected. However, the factory, in its defense, stated that although the Factory Law had been implemented, factories had not actually complied with it. Now that the court has made the above ruling, workers who are injured on the job can legally demand compensation from the factory based on this law. The court's reasoning is transcribed below:

"Since the plaintiff worked as a car repairman in the defendant's factory, matters related to factory repairs are within his job description. The defendant cannot be held responsible simply because of different supervisors. The claim that the belts in the defendant's factory were not replaced after prolonged use is unsubstantiated. Furthermore, witnesses Zhu Weizhang and Tan Xifan testified that the plaintiff was injured because he was careless when handling the belt, not because the belt was defective. It is evident that the plaintiff's injury was not the fault of the defendant, and therefore his claim for compensation for losses is without merit. However, since the plaintiff's right arm was completely severed, resulting in permanent disability, his request for benefits is justified. The plaintiff claims that his daily wage was 85 cents, plus a monthly double wage of 12 yuan and annual bonuses, which, calculated over three years, would amount to 1,900 yuan. However, Article 45, Paragraph 1, Section 2 of the Factory Law states that disability benefits cannot exceed the average wage for more than three years. The plaintiff's daily wage and monthly double wage in the defendant's factory were only over 30 yuan, and annual bonuses are not considered wages and cannot be included in the calculation. Therefore, based on the scope defined by the Factory Law, this court orders the defendant to pay the plaintiff 1,000 yuan in benefits as compensation, and the plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. This ruling is made in accordance with Article 82 of the Civil Procedure Law, as stated in the main text."

Our industry should also respect personal integrity and exercise self-restraint. Under no circumstances should we pay unexpected or improper fees that are not officially receipted, to avoid harming ourselves. If any instances of private transactions are discovered, we hope that you will report them with verifiable evidence so that we can report them to the railway authorities for investigation and prosecution in accordance with the law, to assist the Ministry of Railways in its diligent efforts to manage and prevent malfeasance. This notification is hereby issued, and we hope that all members along the two railway lines will take note."
