Shenbao Local Supplement

Commentary

The Downfall of a Warlord 170

— ·Fo·

Zhang Zongchang, known for his "three don't knows" (don't know how many troops, don't know how much money, don't know how many concubines), was stationed in Shandong at the time, and was extremely powerful. The people of Shandong suffered from his tyranny, and to this day, people still turn pale at the mention of his name.

According to reports yesterday, Zhang Zongchang was suddenly attacked at Jinan Station as he was about to leave, and died of serious injuries. Two murderers were arrested on the spot, confessing that they were avenging their father. Alas! The downfall of a warlord is nothing more than this. The saying that "the son of a good doctor often dies of illness, and the son of a good witch often dies by ghosts" means that "one's own way is used to treat one's own body," which is a principle of retribution that never fails.

However, I don't need to delve into Zhang's past deeds, as the world has its own judgment. I don't need to delve into them, and I don't need to make profound comments on Zhang's death, as the inside story is not yet clear. However, there is one commendable thing in Zhang's life:

"I am Zhang Zongchang, not Zhang Bangchang." This kind of heroic tone is as if I can hear his voice. Zhang Zongchang was also extremely opposed to the puppet behavior in the Northeast. Compared with Zheng Xiaoxu, Xi Qia, Zang Shiyi and other foxes and dogs who willingly helped the rebels and acted as accomplices, he was still slightly better.

When Zhang was assassinated, one of the assassins shouted, "I am Zheng Jicheng, son of Zheng Jinsheng, avenging my father!" Then he jumped off the railway and fired several shots at Zhang's head. This assassin is also rare. Ordinary assassins often refuse to reveal their names after assassinating others, but Zheng Jicheng announced his name first, and he is also worthy of being a hero.

Since ancient times, heroes have cherished heroes, and villains have cherished villains. They should not kill each other, but when enemies meet, they are especially clear. Zhang's straightforward words met Zheng Jicheng, who was also straightforward. They met on a narrow road, and Zhang Zongchang had no choice but to die at the hands of his enemy.

Some say that Zhang Zongchang's trip must have involved other activities, and was not as reported in the newspapers, dealing with property disputes. Then I will not bother with this dead account.

Literature and Art

Looking at the Sea in Wusong 171

— ·Ming· ·Ju· ·Shi·

Where do the vast waves end? Only many ships are seen. Banners and symbols are placed horizontally across the sea, wind and clouds rise and fall on the waves. Turning back to look for the old country, the eyes are full of soldiers and weapons. This is the snow in front of the door, how can it sweep the streets?

Feeling Inspired by the Sound of Crickets in Autumn

The scorching sun fades, and a cool breeze rises gently. The clear sky has no clouds, and the autumn moon is a bright crescent. Holding a book, I sit in my thatched hut, and the shadow of the osmanthus tree moves in the sky. I listen to the chirping of crickets on the mossy steps, endlessly chattering. Like enemies of their own kind, they are not afraid to defend themselves. High and low, they wield their claws and teeth, shouting from the bamboo groves. Risking life and death in a single gamble, these tiny insects are restless. One defeat loses all prestige, one victory makes them arrogant. Humans often kill each other, how much different are they? I will also seal your mouth to avoid laughing at the righteous birds.

Science

Paper Pottery 172

— ·Xiao· ·Tao·

Everyone! Before reading this article on paper pottery, please think for a moment, if there were no paper in the world today, how much hardship would people feel! Since paper is an indispensable item, how can we not know how it is made? Now I will write the manufacturing and history of paper below:

In ancient China, there was no paper. In order to record the things that had been done and felt, so as not to forget, bamboo was cut into slips, and lacquer was used to write on the slips. There were also writings on silk, animal skins, or the trunks of plants, and carvings on stone slabs, and even more foolish ways of recording events by tying knots. These methods of recording events were extremely inconvenient. During the reign of Emperor He of the Later Han Dynasty, there was a man from Guiyang named Cai Lun. He was very intelligent and felt that writing in this way was too inconvenient, so he used materials such as hemp fiber, rags, rice straw, and reeds to try to make paper. Where there's a will, there's a way, and his invention was indeed successful. His contribution to mankind is truly great!

Among Western countries, the Egyptians were the earliest to make paper.

Their raw material for making paper was reeds. The paper made from reeds was coarse and thick, and it was difficult to write on. After the method of papermaking in our country was introduced to their country, Austria, Germany, Sweden and other countries opened paper factories and conducted research, and from then on, the method of papermaking in our country spread throughout Europe.

The raw materials for Western papermaking are wood, rags and waste paper. They put the purchased rags and waste paper into a cutting machine to chop them up, put them into a soil removal machine to remove the soil from the waste paper and wash them clean. Then they put them into a large iron pot to cook them thoroughly, remove the original pigments, and put them into a bleaching tank, adding bleaching powder to bleach them. After bleaching, they add glue and chalk (chalk can increase the weight of the paper), then put them into a filter, pass them through a metal mesh to directly press them, to remove moisture, and put them into a dryer, so that the pressed paper is dried and comes out. The reason why Chinese paper breaks when written on with ink is because no glue is added during papermaking. The paper made in our country is too little, and it is often in short supply. Only the sales of Western paper have invisibly increased. Furthermore, because China cannot manufacture its own machines and cannot make full use of domestic raw materials, the paper produced is coarse and rough, neither beautiful nor suitable for writing on both sides with pencils or fountain pens. Although brush can be used, if the ink is too light, it will seep the words into a blob of ink; if it is too thick, it will stick and you cannot write. Therefore, buyers feel that Western paper is cheap, strong and durable, and they scramble to buy and use foreign paper. This leakage has become particularly large, which is a major event that deserves our special attention!

According to a survey report, the value of paper imported by Japan alone is about 2,074,096 taels per year. Such a huge leakage is truly frightening!

Society Improvement Discussion Society

Research on Whether Men and Women are Equal Now 173

— ·Jin· ·Men·

Equality between men and women: Equality between men and women: It has been shouted for more than twenty years since the change of dynasty. May I ask whether women are now equal to men? If this question is studied carefully, I am afraid that the "not yet" component is more than the "already" component! Before I study this question, I must first ask what exactly constitutes that men and women have already reached equality. This is difficult to answer at once, and can be divided into "broad" and "narrow" meanings. "Narrowly" means equality in all treatments between men and women, and "broadly" includes equality in all treatments and positions between men and women.

Equality in treatment between men and women certainly exists in European and American countries. The old Chinese concepts of "men roam and women hide," "three obediences and four virtues," and "seven grounds for divorce" were extremely unequal, but they have long been naturally eliminated due to the opening up of the country and the eastward spread of European customs. Women are indeed much more liberated than before now, but it cannot be said that they are already equal to men.

Especially with regard to the issue of male-female relationship, it is the most unequal in treatment. Men can have multiple wives, but women can only have one husband. Men can go whoring outside, but women cannot commit adultery at home. Men can remarry immediately after their wives die, and it is very appropriate, but women, although they can also remarry after their husbands die, are annoyed by the difficulties of their parents-in-law and the criticism of relatives and neighbors. It seems that the word "chastity" is used exclusively for women and has nothing to do with men, which is extremely unequal.

However, on the one hand, society shouts loudly for equality between men and women, and on the other hand, it binds them in this way. Why is it so contradictory? This is because women are not yet economically independent and still rely on men for their lives. Old women are certainly like this, but even new women are not much different. Regarding equality in all positions for women, I am afraid that even European and American countries have not reached this level, let alone our country. Because in several national governments, except for a few women in small positions and as members of parliament, there are absolutely no women elected or appointed as prime ministers or ministers, it can also be known that it is very difficult to achieve equal status for women in positions with men.

As for which of the two parties, men and women, is a plaything and who is a slave, this is relative and can be said of both. Men treat new women as playthings, and new women are also treating men as playthings. Men treat old women as slaves, and now new women, who take the money their husbands earn with hard work to go shopping, watch movies, and go to parks, are also treating men as beasts of burden!

A Corner of Society

A Strange Thing 174

— ·Ying· ·Dai·

The day before yesterday, when I came back from Songjiang, I walked through Avenue Road. I accidentally discovered a strange thing. A man in a Western suit, his age was about thirty years old, was holding a child in his arms. This child was only about one year old, and from his small face, it could be determined that his body was unhealthy, perhaps he was sick? Maybe it was a congenital deficiency! The man in the Western suit was holding the child in one hand, and a stack of small red paper bags in the other hand.

In front of him was a middle-aged woman of about the same age as him. In form, they were of course a couple. Her face clearly revealed a kind of melancholy color, frowning, without the slightest smile, leading her husband and child, along the sidewalk beside the road, walking from east to west.

Many people surrounded them to watch the fun. Curiosity urged me, and I couldn't help but stop to see what was going on. I learned that the woman stopped at the door of each house, stopped, and said a few words to the owner. The people in that house put one or two copper coins into the small red paper bag she was holding. The woman handed the bag with money to her husband, and at the same time, she exchanged an empty bag in her husband's hand, and went to another house to ask for copper coins.

Under my eyes, it was really inexplicable. They were a couple who looked very upper-class. Why did they want to ask people for money? The people around were laughing, maybe they were just as puzzled as I was, and some were commenting. Later, I asked the people next to me and learned that they were asking for longevity money, wanting to ask from a hundred families, because the child was sick. Longevity money is to suppress evil spirits and can drive away evil gods and ghosts.

This is really a strange thing. It is so difficult for a beggar to ask people for one or two copper coins, and most people still refuse to give it. But when the couple asked for longevity money, people were very generous in digging into their pockets to give them. In less than an hour, a hundred red bags were filled with copper coins, and then they returned from the original route.

Because I saw them asking for longevity money, it made me have many feelings. In our hometown, the generally ignorant and foolish people, when their children are sick, do not go to see a doctor, but specialize in seeking immortal prescriptions and asking Taoist priests. How can wooden people see a doctor, and how can Taoist priests eliminate demons? As a result, the general small citizens suffer the disaster of death. Unexpectedly, even the intellectual class in the city is so superstitious. From the surface, the man in the Western suit and the woman wearing leather shoes are clearly from the intellectual class, but when their child is sick, they do not go to see a doctor, but use longevity money to suppress evil spirits, isn't it a joke! Under such circumstances, I don't know when the seeds of Chinese superstition will be completely eradicated and eliminated!

Family Education

Chinese Motherhood 175

— ·Ren·

Zhang's wife and the concubine's son are playing in the patio next door. The son of the wife takes advantage of the fact that his mother has great power and often bullies the son of the concubine. But the son of the concubine is also a child, how can he willingly suffer humiliation? Naturally, these two innocent, lively children often quarrel, and even twist into a ball, hitting each other with their small feet and small hands. Because they feel wronged, their hearts are filled with grievances, and the only way to vent is to cry. So the crying reaches the ears of the wife. She hurried over, without distinguishing right from wrong, and slapped the son of the concubine's mouth a few times first, then hugged her son to the street door, comforting him, "Baby, don't cry, Daddy will buy you a foreign doll when he comes back." But he still cried, until his mother came back from the foreign goods store with a foreign doll in her hand, her little baby smiled through tears, holding the foreign doll, as if forgetting what had just happened.

Over there, the son of the concubine was slapped in the mouth, of course, he cried even harder. The concubine, angered, hugged him to the pavilion and locked the door to let him cry, but she did not comfort him, but used a threatening tone, "Son, do you still want to cry? Be careful that foreigners catch you! The day before yesterday, the A'guan next door was caught by yellow-haired, blue-eyed foreign devils for crying and had his eyes dug out to make meat buns." The son of the concubine did not finish listening, and climbed over in fright to hide his small face in his mother's arms. For a long time, he still coughed up resentful gasps from his weak trachea.

Such a scene is almost what I see every day when I come back from work, and my heart is filled with pain and sorrow. I thought: Is this how Chinese motherhood teaches children? Oh, I understand! It turns out that the Chinese mentality of "liking foreign goods" and "worshipping and fearing foreigners" is deeply planted in the weak hearts of their children by the mothers in their innocent childhood.

Childhood

My Childhood 176

— ·Zhu· ·Lai·

丨Childhood Memories丨

How precious childhood is, it has passed like flowing water! But I am a big child who likes children. As long as I see their innocent attitude, I am happily fascinated and deeply admire the happiness of childhood. However, there is no hope of reversing time, and God cannot give me to be a child again! This semester, I am in charge of the lowest level arithmetic class, and I am closer to the little brothers and sisters: touching their smiling apple faces, holding their slender little hands, and seeing them wearing beautiful clothes: so I feel that children are really cute.

XXXXXXXXX

Recalling my golden childhood, in the second year of school, I was always naughty in the temple every day. Once, I walked into the side room of the Dacun Temple and boldly took a clay dog and smashed it to pieces. After resting for two days, I got a serious illness. During the illness, according to my mother, "You keep shouting that the little-footed woman and old lady are coming again!" Therefore, I was so anxious that I couldn't sleep or eat, making vows and hiring doctors: I was so busy!" After resting for a week, I recovered from the illness. My mother brought a basket of pancakes and a large pile of incense candles and ingots, and solemnly led me to the temple to worship the wife.

Around the age of eight, every year at the turn of April and May, I went to the bamboo garden with naughty children to find bird nests. If I found small birds like whiteheads, I would be very happy to raise them, as if treating them as small companions. But after a long time, they were either swallowed by cats or starved to death. So I dug a small pond and buried them inside. At the same time, I inserted some fresh flowers and weeds on the mud surface, and sprinkled a bag of tears from my eyes, which was not an unhappy memorial!

When the hot summer arrives, every day I get up early, drag a pair of torn cloth shoes, and carry a very long bamboo pole, running east and west to roll up spider webs. Secondly, I take a small basket and go to the willow trees on the river bank to pick up cicada pupae. After picking them up, I string them one by one on thin white lines and hang them in my mother's room. As soon as the clanging sound of the candy seller comes, I smile and take them to exchange for candy.

At the age of twelve, it was a year of prosperous gambling with my little friends. On a long road that I traveled every day, I drew a ladder-shaped boundary to play the game of throwing copper coins. As soon as I saw my father coming, I scrambled to escape straight to the temple. After school, I secretly went to the Zhang family in the east house and sat on the gate, happily playing with cigarette cards. Like me, I was repeatedly defeated, but the interest in gambling never decreased!

From the age of six, I liked to accumulate large Qing white copper coins, string them together one by one, and put them in my mother's drawer very preciously. By the year I was eleven, I had accumulated five hundred large copper coins. It was really happy, and from that year, I lent eighty copper coins to the old man, the wine fairy on the house, and every year in the tenth month of the lunar calendar, I received one hundred and fifty texts of interest, which was really satisfying.

XXXXXXXXX

This work is narrated nakedly. I deeply feel that in my childhood, I was also a naughty child with the first character in the world. Now, I have some whiskers under my chin, and the biggest child in my family is fully eight years old. Reflecting on the past, it is really a world of difference, like two different people. However, I only hope that an innocent soul will not pass away with the years.
